and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細觀察 , 特別是塑膠瓶 , 大部分都只能降級回收 , 或是燒完 , 或是運到中國去 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	被降級回收並轉化成更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶的話 , 就不會再是塑膠瓶了 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個重大的議題
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們研究的另一件事是要求大家去思考 , 就是我們在 「 減量、再利用、回收 」 前面加上第四個r , 也就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	無論何時都要拒絕使用即丟的塑膠品
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是存在的 ; 有些是非常老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在收集了這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用的不是glad而是裝上發泡的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我是在為自己和我的家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要找到一個不銹鋼瓶、玻璃瓶非常容易 , 如果你在旅行時 , 你已經忘記帶個不銹鋼瓶裝滿水或過濾水 , 而不是買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想我在這裡想對在座各位說的──我知道你們對於這個議題有很大的了解──這在海洋是個很大的問題 , 但這是個我們身為消費者、我們能解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以通過提高人們的認知 , 來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 無論何時 , 要選擇單一使用塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這首詩的潮汐切成我們的海洋 , 這樣做 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	帕蒂馬斯在麻省理工學院的實驗室發表演說 , 帕納•米茨在ted發表演說中 , 戴著投影機 , 用投影機在和環境中深深互動的方式 。 想像 「 少數民族報告 」 接著 , 有些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	demo , 設計 , 界面設計 , 科技
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂馬斯和帕納小姐示範第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很感興趣 , 像是我們能否演化出或發展出第六感的感覺 , 一種能夠讓我們在存在某處更便宜、更容易取得新陳代碼或訊息的感覺 , 或許可以幫助我們做出正確的決定 , 做出我們要面對的各種問題 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會說 , 嗯 , 現今的手機不就已經這麼做了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted這裡遇見一個人這是最頂級的網絡網絡地點 , 當然 , 在一年中你不會甩到某人的手然後說: 「 你能在我拿出手機和谷歌時握住你一下嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或是當你到超市 , 站在那個大型的廁所衛生紙走道上 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 到一個網站 , 試著決定不同的衛生紙中哪些是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們並不容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 能夠協助我們做出最佳的決定 , 決定下一步要做什麼、採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組已經研發出一系列的發明 , 讓我們能用簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 且不用要求使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡就是要揭開我們最新努力的成果 , 目前為止大部分的成功成果 , 這仍然是個過程 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我現在穿著這套裝置我們有點像是把它和一些零件結合在一起就在現場 , 順道一提 , 這裝置現在的成本只有350美元
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著攝影機 , 只是個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜帶 , 電池動力的投影系統 , 配上一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件是我口袋裡的手機 , 用來當作通訊和計算的設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中我們看到我的學生 , 帕納•米崔 , 他是正在實施並設計整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何平面前 , 開始用他的手來與前面投影的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤這四隻顯著的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他穿著你可能認得的簡單標記瓶 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	而攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且辨識出他的任何手勢舉例來說 , 他可以直接到一個長灘的地圖 , 放大等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統也辨識出具象徵性的手勢 , 例如 「 照相 」 這個手勢 , 然後照張相 , 呈現出你面前的一切 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室後 , 他可以走到任何一面牆前投射他拍下的照片 , 分析並整理出來 , 再利用所有自然的手勢等等 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前你們有些人可能也在這裡看過傑夫•漢或你們有些人會想: 「 這不像微軟的平面電腦嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也會用自然的手勢來互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的不同點是 , 你可以用任何平面 , 你可以走到任何平面前 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西是可以用的 , 並與這些投影的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 也可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要差異是 , 它完全是移動式的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	還有另一個更重要的不同點是大量生產不會比現今的手機來得費用更高 , 而且不會成為更大的包裝形狀 , 可能比我脖子上穿的這個版本還要時髦的多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除了讓你們一些人活出你的幻想 , 像是在《關鍵報告》中 , 湯姆克魯斯 , 我們對這個裝置感到很興奮的原因是 , 它的作用可能是這第六感裝置 , 能夠提供你關於眼前事物的資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納進入超市去購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一樣產品 , 系統可以辨認出他拿起的產品 , 用的是影像辨識或是標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘色燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 ,
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 根據他的個人標準 , 這種選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能會想用最漂白的衛生紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他能取得亞馬遜書局的評分 , 會直接投影到書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜這本書得到很好的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	因此 , 帕納翻閱這本書 , 就能看到更多關於這本書的資訊 , 像是他最喜歡的評論家等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到特定的一頁 , 找到我們朋友的專家寫的註解 , 會給他一點額外的資訊 , 知道那一頁有什麼 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙──它永遠不用過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以取得你正在閱讀的事件的影片註解--你可以得到最新的體育分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個更具爭議性的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與某人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個字雲 , 標籤關聯著那個人的字 , 在他們的部落格和個人的網頁上 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這種情況下 , 學生對相機有興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你前往機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的航班延誤 , 登機門已改變 , 諸如此類 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道現在的時間是什麽就如同在你手臂上畫一個手錶一樣簡單
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這是我們目前正在開發的第六感能夠讓我們無縫接觸到關於我們可能遇到的一切的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 他真的 , 像我說的 , 是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去三個月中睡得多 , 其實是睡得好 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友大概也不太高興他 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但還不完美 , 還差得遠了 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 , 或許十年之後我們會帶著植入腦內的終極第六感來到這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichaelwafi有一個很強大的友誼誕生於不可思議的損失 。 rodriguez的兒子在2001年9月11日受到殺害 ; elwafi的兒子zacariasmousoui被定罪 , 在那些攻擊中 , 並且被定罪為一個生命的標誌 。 希望找到和平 , 這兩個媽媽們都了解並尊敬 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911療癒:那些發現寬恕的母親、友誼的母親
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉絲•羅德里格茲:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們擁有大多數人認為是非比尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們卻感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次知道我的兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否已經死了 , 直到36小時後 ,
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼事以我們兒子的名義--我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到──然而 , 透過震驚、可怕的震驚 , 以及我們生命中的可怕的爆炸──真的 , 我們沒有要報仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖攻擊的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判死刑如果罪名成立的話 , 我和我的丈夫對公開反對這條規定 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些和透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者家屬一起合作 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她的兒子被指起 , 我心想: 「 這真是個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天我希望當我更堅強時 , 能遇到那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍在深深的哀傷之中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上就得到了同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們得知她兒子被指控的事 , 她沒有得到那份同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦與我的相同之處
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年11月認識 , 現在aicha會告訴你這是怎麼一回事 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我接觸到受害者父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭認識 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 看著她
she was the only mother in the group .	她是那個小組裡唯一的媽媽
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是一位母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我作為一個媽媽很痛苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 ,
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 十六歲時失去了第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以zacarias的故事真的太過重 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子而哭 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 不知道他是否受到折磨
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的痛苦對其他女性來說是很正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的婦女 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手一起做些事
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性這是為我們、為我們女人、為我們的孩子
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 ,
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年青的穆斯林女孩說話 , 這樣她們就不接受不和她們的意願結婚 , 非常年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 並且避免她們跟我一樣的結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會在你們面前
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha身上學到好多 , 從那天開始我們和其他家庭成員第一次見面-這是一個高度保障的私人會議 , 因為當時是二零二零二年十一月 , 而且 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時國家裡的超級愛國主義---我們這些家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	後來她很緊張
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為何想見她 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們到底想要什麼呢 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字或其他東西之前 , 我們就已經擁抱和哭泣了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們圍成一個圓圈 , 靠著支援和協助 , 從人們在這種和解過程中所經歷的 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我有多遺憾為你們的家庭所發生的事 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道這是怎樣的受苦 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該受到公平的審判及懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以那種方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想說 , 這是一場破冰船 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	發生的狀況是 , 我們都說出了自己的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分來連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	到了下午完結的時候----大概是午餐後的三小時--我們感覺好像彼此認識了一輩子 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 是一個女人 , 不單只是在現狀和當時的情況下 , 能夠如此大方 , 及正在對她兒子做了什麼 , 還有她所過的生活 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼艱苦的生活 , 和我的文化和環境完全不同 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種很特別的連結 , 我很重視這個連結 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這些都是因為害怕對方 , 但做出那一步 , 接著我發現: 「 嘿 , 這沒有這麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能跟誰見面 , 我不知道 , 或我和別人如此不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你的結論有幾個字嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 ,
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說 , 我們必須試著去認識其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 。

you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。

this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界太多無法取得乾淨飲用水 。 工程師麥克.普里查對這件事做了些貢獻 , 發明了攜帶式救生過濾器 , 它能在幾秒鐘內製造出最佳飲用水 。 2009年tedglobal的展示品 。

i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想講幾點
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受著在會議中為你們提供的水量 , 過去幾天以來
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得那是從安全源頭
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣一個電源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	然後統計數字會說你們之中有一半的人現在患上了腹瀉 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我過去談過很多關於統計 , 和提供所有人安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎無法通過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	這是因為 , 用當前的想法 , 問題的規模似乎太大了以致於無法思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關閉:我們、政府、和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想讓各位看看 , 透過不同的思考 , 這個問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 自從我開始演講以來 , 全球又有一萬三千人患有腹瀉 。
and four children have just died .	而四個孩子剛剛死去
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我很生氣 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我 , 和你們一樣 , 大部分的人都坐著 , 那是2004年聖誕節的隔天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯摧毀的消息 , 一邊在電視上播出 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	隨後的日子 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的很困擾我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	然後 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風襲擊了美國 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 咱們來看看他們能做到什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你們知道要花五天才能把水送到超市嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相開槍 , 為了電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我就決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月裡 , 還有 , 在我的廚房裡 , 很常讓我太太很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型 , 我終於想到了這個 , 生命安全瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌就差不多200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以它一定會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifesaver濾水孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	沒有什麼能穿透 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好了 , 我來示範一下
would you like to see that ?	你們想看嗎 ?

so someone's done that up .	有人做到了 。

but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我在想 , 要知道 , 如果我們身處在孟加拉的洪水區中間 , 水不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以我去找了一些東西來加進去
and this is from my pond .	而這是從我的池塘來的
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞一下吧 , 攝影師先生
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們就把它倒進去 。

the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶的效果相當簡單 。

okay . there we go .	好了 。 來了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些泵 , 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這就是所有必要的了
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	我一跳水就會排出無菌的飲用水 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快點了 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	來了 , 請注意電

there you go chris .	來了克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	味道如何 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯在接下來的節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 。 世界各地有上千人在使用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	可以維持6 , 000公升
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用故障安全技術 , 系統會自行關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把地毯拿出來 , 換一個新的進去 ,
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	對另外六千公升也好 。
so let's look at the applications .	我們來看看它的應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統的危機 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 幾個星期後 , 我們設立營地 ,
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到營地取用安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在一個難民營 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病會傳播出去 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會自行繁衍
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思考 , 再運送這些資料 , 人們可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 並開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	其實 , 這並不需要天然災害才有用 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊思維 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 太昂貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你用計算機計算時 , 你的數目是 「 無奈 」 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這是 「 不同的思維 」 部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程去做 , 不如利用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費淡化水 , 運送到那邊 , 然後傾倒在山地、河川、以及溪流中 。
and where do people live ? near water .	而人們住在哪裡 ? 鄰近水源的地方 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的只是讓它變得很不穩定 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以使用一種
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在一個jerry的罐子裡
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這樣就會處理25 , 000公升的水 。 這足夠一個四人家庭使用三年 。
and how much does it cost ?	而要付出多少代價呢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約只需半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 透過換個角度思考 , 再用水來處理 , 母親和孩子不用再每天步行四小時來收集自己的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的電源取得
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只用了八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	為了說明這個問題英國政府每年花約120億英鎊在國外援助上
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	靠著200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	因此 , 每年因此受苦的三十五億人以及每年因此死亡的兩百萬名孩子將會活著
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashdowns說 , 我們正處於歷史中 , 權力正在改變以往不曾有過的方式 。 在tedxbrussel的演說中 , 他推出三個全球重大的轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashdown:全球勢力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩這麼寫道這是一個非常有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	它是在1930年代 , 據說邱吉爾的大腦迴響 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這樣說的: " 在夏日的山丘上 , 帶著小溪散落 , 我聽到了遠方的鼓聲 , 鼓聲像夢裡的聲音 , 遠處 , 接近低沉 , 大聲到達地球的道路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物 , 遊行到粉末 , 士兵們很快就死了 。 "
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " 許洛普斯拉夫人 " 寫了一篇a.e.豪斯曼的詩 ,
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼所了解的 , 你也能在尼爾森的交響樂中聽到 , 十九世紀那漫長、炎熱、野蠻的夏天即將要到來 , 我們即將走入歷史上最可怕的一段時間 , 權力改變了 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著騷動 , 常常也是血肉之軀 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我想傳達給各位的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責了 , 如果你願意 , 活在歷史上的那些時刻之一 , 當已經建立起的權力秩序開始改變的那一刻 , 世界上新的權力開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	現在我們看到的這些 , 非常清楚的 , 幾乎總是高度動亂的時代 , 非常艱困的時代 , 而且常常也是血腥時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順道一提 , 每個世紀發生一次
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會主張 , 上次發生這種狀況 , 那是豪斯曼所感覺到的 , 也是邱吉爾也感覺到的 , 當權力從老國傳到歐洲的舊勢力 , 橫跨大西洋傳到美國的新興強國時 , 這一刻也是美國世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在以前歐洲人的權力真空 , 在上個世紀 , 有兩場血腥的災難 , 這場災難發生在第一部份 , 第二部分:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾以歐洲內戰稱他們為 「 歐洲內戰 」 , 它可能是比較正確的形容方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中一次
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 今天我想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一個 , 前面兩個 , 關於權力的轉移 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些我想參考的新維度 , 從來沒有像現在這樣發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 咱們來談談現今在全世界發生的權力轉移 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	而現在的情況是 , 在某種意義上 , 非常恐怖 , 因為這從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到希臘通過羅馬的橫向轉變 , 以及在歐洲文明期間發生的權力移轉 , 但我們看到的情況稍有不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只是國與國之間的橫向移動 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直地移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今的情況是 , 被賦予的權力 , 受到責任的牽制 , 受到法律的牽制 , 在這個國家的制度下 , 現在已被大量地遷移到全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力我們談論的是全球化的市場 , 但實際上 , 卻是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級 , 權力在哪裡被賦予法律的權力 , 在國際舞台上則否 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台上 , 現在有著全球的權力:網際網路的權力 , 衛星廣播的權力 , 金錢的權力 , 改變了大筆金錢的權力 , 現在有32倍的資金 , 供應給金錢的權力 , 應該要有大筆的資金 , 如果你喜歡的話 , 可以說是金融的策略 , 最近常常有的多國企業經費發展預算 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些居住在一個全球化的空間 , 一個大多都不受管制 , 不受法律規範的管制 , 而且人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	此時此刻 , 強而有力的出現了 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	這總是適合那些有最強權力的人在沒有約束力的情況下運作的人 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 法律所沒有被管制的空間 , 不僅僅是被那些你想要的國際貿易、網路 , 等等 。 同時也是你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的啟示是 , 即使你是地球上最有權力的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些空間的人 , 能夠攻擊你甚至在九月的最具代表性的早晨 , 攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約四百萬美金中有百分之六十拿去資助911恐怖攻擊911事件發生時其實是通過雙子星大樓的機構911摧毀
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也會用這個空間──大眾旅遊、網路、衛星廣播的空間 , 來打破它們的毒害 , 也就是摧毀我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力的治理要跟著走 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	而如果我相信是這樣的 , 我們這個時代的其中一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的一個挑戰就是把統治者帶上國際舞台 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信未來數十年前我們將有更大、更小的動盪 , 或多或少的動盪 , 我們能夠達到那個目標:把統治者帶上國際舞台 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立一些全球民主制度 ,
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 各位先生女士 , 我自己的觀點是 , 推動更多的聯合國機構是不可能辦到的 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個手段 , 來合法地將國際行動合理化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但談到全球公共場所的管理時 , 我猜想 , 要透過更多聯合國機構的創立 , 不會發生這樣的事 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它實際上會發生在強權聚集在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的制度 , 以條約為基礎的協議 , 來統治全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你去看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全是以條約為基礎的組織 , 然而 , 強勢到能夠撐住最強大的 , 美國 , 若有必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:奮鬥的起點是創立一個合約為底的組織
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在我們知道 , 我們得要建立一個能夠把統治權帶到金融空間的機構來做理財推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團g20會議 , 一個以約定為基礎的機構
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題了 , 我們等一下再來談它 , 那就是 , 如果你把最強大的力量集合在一起 , 做以條約為基礎的制度 , 來填補政府的空間 , 那麼 , 弱小的怎麼辦 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下就會回到這問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你比起亂流來得容易 , 那麼我們的成功取決於我們把合理的統治權帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	請注意這一切的開始 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要向觀眾這樣討論這件事 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 同時它也橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 一直以來文明都聚集在海洋四周 , 地中海附近最先到達的 , 是比較近期的西方國家在大西洋的權力附近 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的基本轉移 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離那些聚集在大西洋岸邊的國家 , 到太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這始於經濟實力 , 但始終是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 會發生在世界上其他不斷增長的勢力 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得這其實不是西方國家之間的轉變 ; 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於它的價值 , 就是美國會繼續留在地球上最強的國家在接下來的十年 , 十五年 , 但她掌握的權力背景現在已經徹底改變了 ; 它已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正從五十年、最不尋常的歷史來看 , 在這個時代 , 我們有一個非常獨特的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一個羅盤都需要指南或反對它 , 它的位置必須由華盛頓指揮 , 一個被大巨帝給佔領的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這在歷史上卻不常見
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在發生的是更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你也開始看到多極化世界的出現
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是我們這個世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強權的國家 , 但他們會是越來越多極化的世界中最強的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	然後你會開始看到其他的權力建設中心在中國雖然我認為中國要達到偉大的目標並不順利
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	一切都會很糟糕 , 因為中國在自由化她的經濟之後 , 開始將她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論對象的一個主題
you see india , you see brazil .	你看印度、巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 世界看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一個英國的外交大國秘書長 , 大法官坎寧 , 以前形容它為 「 歐洲人的權力音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	當時有一個平衡 , 一邊是五邊的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國人總是把玩弄平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎跟柏林合作 , 英國就和維也納及羅馬合作 , 提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在請注意 , 在這被單一強權對立的世界主導的時期 , 你有固定的聯盟──北約組織、華約組織 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固有的權力對立 , 意味著固定的聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力的多重兩極化就表示要轉移、改變盟友關係 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們即將進入的世界 , 我們將看到 , 我們的同盟國沒有固定的連結 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 英國外交大臣曾經說過: 「 英國人有共同的利益 , 但卻沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們也會看到 , 即使在西方國家也會伸出援手 , 不得不伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 與他人結盟 , 如果我們想要在這個世界上完成事情 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 光是西方國家是不夠的 ; 我們必須把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方世界最後一次嘗試自己做的時候 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是我們已經到達了400年年底的開始我說400年 , 因為這是鄂圖曼帝國的結束在西方國家權力 , 西方國家的制度和西方價值
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 到目前為止 , 如果西方國家齊心協力 , 就能在世界上的每個角落提出和反對的意見 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以最後一次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行、國際貨幣基金組織等組織共同解決的問題 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給他人
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造出g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做出一個預測 , 這可能更驚人 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑400年後 , 西方的權力已經夠用了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	有人對我說: 「 中國人當然永遠不會參與佔領世界各地多邊調停的調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔可以嗎 ? 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷帽下 , 在藍色旗幟下服務 , 在聯合國的指令下服務呢 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大海軍陸戰隊在處理索馬利海盜的議題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍陸戰隊的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然他們是 , 他們是商人的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	想維持航道開放 ,
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些和我們不分享價值觀的人做生意 , 但與此時此刻 , 我們有共同的興趣 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看現在正在興起的世界
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	接下來是第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們的現代世界 , 由於互聯網 , 由於人們一直以來談論的各式各樣的話題 , 每件事都與每件事有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是相互關聯的 , 以個人的身份 , 在某種程度上 , 這是從未發生過的 , 也從未發生過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的相互關係 , 一直都存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的相互關係
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切關在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到了豬流感 , 24小時後對查爾斯•德•蓋爾的機場出問題了 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下台了 , 整場崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原上有火 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都已深深地彼此緊密相連 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	意思就是 , 一個國家獨自行動 , 不和他人連結 , 不和他人合作 , 不再是個可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的作為都不受限於自己 , 也不足以控制國家本身的領土 , 因為國家外部的影響已經開始影響到他們內在的情況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我年輕時是英國小帝國戰爭時的軍人 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時候 , 我國家的辯護重點只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多堅強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時候敵人就在城牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人卻在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在如果我想談談我的國家安全的辯解 , 我必須跟衛生署談談因為傳染疾病對我們的健康造成威脅我得和農業局談談因為糧食安全對我的國家造成威脅我得和工業部談談因為高科技公共設施的不足對我們敵人的攻擊行動正如我們從網路戰爭所看到的我得和內政部談談因為我們進入我們國家的房子的人對發生在倫敦七七七七七七歲的都感到恐懼
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再是對軍人和國防部的重視 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	有能力將其制度鎖在一起
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴了你一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直架構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式縱向階層 , 專門處理工作任務 , 指揮結構已經完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在企業你知道我們這個時代的典範架構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是這個網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網絡網絡有重要性的能力 , 不論是在你的政府內部或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是第三個法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	對了 , 別問我第一定律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明那些 ; 第三法則總是比較好聽 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三定律是 , 在現代 , 所有東西都有關連 , 最重要的是你能做什麼 , 是你能和他人做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 無論你是政府 , 還是軍人 , 無論你是商人 , 無論你是生意上的要點 , 你的互聯網 , 你與他人建立關係的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在工業上 ; 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但現在最後一件事
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士 , 就是我們現在被鎖在一起 , 以一種前所未有的方式鎖在一起 , 那也是我們彼此命中注定的情況 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 首當其衝的還是集體的防禦 , 那些主宰我們對國家安全的觀念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 事情是這樣的 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強 , 我就安全了 ; 我的盟國 , 像北約 , 比他們的同盟還強 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	已經不再是這樣了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的相互關聯性進步意味著我與敵人分享我的命運
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	1970年代 , 我還是外交官 , 在日內瓦和蘇聯爭取消費條約時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解 , 我們和他們有著共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著共同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	對於中東和平的一個大障礙就是雙方、以色列 , 以及巴勒斯坦人都不了解他們有集體命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 各位先生女士 , 對於有遠見的人以及詩人的提議會變成我們必須認真看待的公共政策
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我以一首詩作為開場 , 將以一首詩作為結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 送誰的鐘頭給誰 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我也涉入人類 , 不去問誰響鐘 , 都是為了誰響鐘 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對多恩來說 , 一種道德建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們而言 , 我認為 , 對於我們生存的方程式的一部分
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到通往長壽生活的道路 , danbuettner和團隊研究世界的 " 藍色慢活區 " , 這些社區的長者和vim和vigor在tedxtc分享了九種常見的飲食和生活方式的習慣 , 使得他們在100歲以上奮鬥了 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、生命、科學 ,
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100+100 ?
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個丹麥雙胞胎的研究指出 , 一般人的壽命只有一般人的10% , 在特定的生理限制下 , 基因決定了我們的壽命 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他百分之九十是由生活方式決定
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式我們就能得出一個實際長壽的公式
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳配方是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘減肥法或阿特金減肥法
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國農業部的食物金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是 ,
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事情的真相是 , 有許多混淆存在於真正幫助我們活得更長久的東西 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到營養品 , 你該吃嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那這些荷爾蒙或白斑呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	這樣做有目的性嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神層面呢 ? 那我們如何社交 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們研究長壽的方法是與國家地理還有國家老化研究院合作找出四個人口確定地理界線分明的區塊
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把一個專家團隊帶到裡面 , 用方法來處理這些人的所作所為 , 來提煉出跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	講到這 , 最後我要告訴你們精華是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想打破一些常見的迷思長壽的迷思
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一項迷思是 , 如果你很努力地想要活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有五千分之一的人能活到一百歲
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是全美成長最快的人口 , 還是很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們並沒有長壽的計劃
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為一種叫做 " 繁衍成功 " 的產品 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學生活
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱此為 「 循序漸進的成功 」 指的是你有孩子的年齡 , 然後再過一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應就會完全消失 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是隻老鼠、大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 這都是同樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要活到一百歲 , 你不僅得有個很好的生活方式 , 你還得拿到基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二項迷思是 , 有療程可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 或甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想一想 , 有99件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要你的腦袋缺氧幾分鐘腦細胞就會死 , 從不復返
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太硬 , 膝蓋太硬 , 把軟骨弄壞 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用 「 斑塊 」 來開啟 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情可能會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 有t兆個有 「 t 」 的數字 , 我們在這裡談的是國債 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就會自己轉動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每次它們自己轉向那裡就會產生一些傷害 。 而傷害會累積起來 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數增加的速度增長
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像以前 , 我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯 , 我們會用錄音帶做一份複本 , 讓朋友用錄音帶錄音 , 很快的 , 代代相傳 , 錄音帶就聽起來像垃圾一樣 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個六十五歲的人老化的速度 , 比一個十二歲的人快一百二十五倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有辦法減緩老化或停止老化那我在這裡做什麼呢 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事情的真相是 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 比女人多一點點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以在某個時點 , 我們會在桌子上留下12年的美好 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年是我們可以得到
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 牠們大多可以免除慢性病、心臟病、癌症 , 及糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 得到這些消失的最佳方式 , 就是看看世界各地的文化 , 實際體驗的文化 , 人們活到一百歲的比率 , 比我們多出十倍的地方 , 平均壽命多了十幾年 , 中年的死亡率 , 是這個國家中期的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們第一批藍寶地在義大利海岸外約125英哩處 , 薩丁尼亞島上
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫作努奧羅省的地區 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡的男人活得最長壽百歲人瑞的數目大約是美國的十倍
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	在這個地方 , 人們不僅活到一百歲 , 他們還帶著很棒的活力 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍舊騎腳踏車去工作 , 砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十歲的男人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可以追溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是孤立的青銅器時代文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這片土地非常貧瘠 , 大部份都是牧羊人 , 這片土地上常規、低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食多以植物為主 , 以他們可帶到田裡的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做 " 卡達麥香 " 用 " 小麥做的 " , 一種由草食動物製成的乳酪 , 所以乳酪富含omega-3脂肪酸而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自穀物餵養的動物還有一種葡萄酒 , 它的多酚物質含量比全世界任何酒都高三倍
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密在於他們如何組織社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老人的方式
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看一下廣告就知道
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越是平等 , 你就越會得到讚揚的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看不到運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不只讓老邁的父母跟家人更親近還增加了大約四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示這對家庭的小孩也有益處死亡率和患病的比例較低
that's called the grandmother effect .	這就是所謂的奶奶效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球另一端找到了第二片藍色地帶 , 位在東京南方八百英里處 , 位在琉球的阿奇比拉戈山脈上 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北端 , 這是世界長壽的起點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	在這個地方 , 最古老的女性被發現了
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有著世界上最長而無障礙的預期壽命
they have what we want .	他們有我們要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活很久 , 通常在睡眠中死去 , 很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性交之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多約七年的壽命
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍於美國的百歲人瑞
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的蜂群和乳癌發生率 , 美國的大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	以及心血管疾病率的六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化產生了這些數字 , 強烈地表示他們有要教我們什麼 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 用以植物為主的飲食 , 裝滿了蔬菜 , 裡面含有大量顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而他們吃大約八倍多的豆腐比起美國人來說
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起吃什麼更重要的是吃它的方式
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過食 , 如你所知 , 在美國這確實是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們吃盤子比較小 , 所以每次吃的卡路里就比較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其用家庭風格來服務 , 不如用心講話就可以吃了 , 相反地 , 他們在櫃台服務 , 把食物拿走 , 然後帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句三千年的格言 , 我認為是有史以來最棒的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	是孔子發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那個飲食就是大家所知的哈拉、哈蒂、布奇 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這些人在用餐前說的只是一句話 , 提醒他們在吃得飽的時候要先吃到飽 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	這種感覺要花半小時才能從肚子傳到腦袋
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住要停在80%時 , 它能幫助你避免做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但就像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有些社會結構跟長壽相關
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會扼殺
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 一般美國人有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	目前我們只剩下一半
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運地生在琉球你生在一個系統裡讓你自動擁有半打朋友與他們共同生活
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 " moai " 。 如果你在一個模合中 , 你會預期你會分享幸運 , 如果你碰到好運 , 如果事情不好 , 孩子生病 , 父母去世 , 你總是有人在背後支持你 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起九十七年了
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們把成人生活分成兩部分
there is our work life , where we're productive .	這是我們工作的生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這表示退休後要擺輕鬆的椅子 , 或去亞利桑那州打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語裡甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是一個充滿你一生的詞彙 , 這個詞就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	而粗略的翻譯則是 「 早上起床的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的空手道師父來說他的生存價值就是發揚武術
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 漁夫持續一週捕魚 , 一週捕三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際給了我們一份問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們在文化上非常敏銳 , 就是那些把問卷拿出來的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存能力是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上知道為何早上起床
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老女人來說 , 她的生存價值不過就在於她的曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半前被分開 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 抱著一個曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣子 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	然後她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像飛躍上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是很棒的一個想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我去找美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	我們看了一段時間明尼蘇達的草原那裡百歲人瑞的比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了
so , we turned to the data again .	於是 , 我們再次轉向資料
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們找到了美國最長壽的族群 , 其中有七天的愛冒險家集中在加州的羅馬林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派教徒是保守派的方法論者
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們把安息日從星期五日落到星期六日出
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱此為 「 二十四小時的庇護 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	而且他們還遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們的非凡長壽 , 相對來說 ,
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 女性平均壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位冒險家女士而言 , 他們的預期壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯他們預期能多活十一年比起美國同伴來說
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很驚人的研究 。 而且我認為這句話也很特別地說明了這個藍色慢活區計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共同點就是一套非常小的生活習慣他們一生中大部份時間都遵從儀式
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接取自聖經中的飲食 ,
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀第一章第二十九節上帝談到豆腐和種子另一節則是綠色植物很明顯少了肉
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個庇護時間
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每個禮拜24小時不管他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 小孩需要被帶著走 , 他們停下一切 , 專注於他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 宗教裡的 " 天行 "
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這股力量並不是偶爾可以完成的 , 這股力量是每週都要一輩子完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派教徒往往跟其他的冒險家混交
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家派對 , 你不會看到有人在揮動jimbeam或打滾一個聯合體 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	反之 , 他們是在談他們的下一個自然步行、交換食譜 , 以及 , 是的 , 他們會祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化造就了埃爾斯沃•偉倫這樣的人 ,
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁 , 但當包商想要六千美元來建造一個隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了那類的錢 , 我自己就能辦到 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天他都在外頭鏟水泥把竿子拖到附近
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料的 , 也許第四天他會在手術室裡
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上這個人做的開心手術
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲的他每個月仍然做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在103歲 , 是個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 丟出強壯的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實生活在雙子城市這裡
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從舉重開始
she rides her bicycle .	騎腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在1994年根部塞維爾角 , 沿著聖貝納迪諾高速公路下落 , 在那裡她仍然自願參與7個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參與十九次冒險活動 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一一個你見到的人他騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠沒有防曬霜
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴你 , 沒有任何探險比搭便車的甲板還令人痛心 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中的共通點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼呢 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們想辦法把它歸還到9 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經做了兩次藍色慢活區的探險 , 都是真的 , 而這些常見的分類學家也做到了 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一項 , 我即將提出一項異議 , 沒有一項運動 , 至少我們是這麼看待運動的 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們設定了他們的生活 , 這樣他們才會持續推動身體的活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人每天都起床三十或四十次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯向上 ,
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店或教堂或去朋友家都要走路
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利性 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以推動 , 去做院子或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要攪拌一塊蛋糕 , 他們會用手
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跟跑步機一樣會燃燒卡路里 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意的身體活動時 , 是他們享受的東西 。 他們會走路 , 唯一證實可以延遲認知能力下降的路徑 , 而且他們都往往有個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式生活所以他們有正確的人生觀
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間慢慢往下移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的教徒祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人的祖先受到威脅
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你很趕時間或是壓力很大時 , 這就會引發一種稱為 「 發炎反應 」 的東西 , 它和一切都息相關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢個十五分鐘 , 就會把那發炎狀態轉變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們的用語是達到目的 , ikikigai , 就像琉球人的用詞 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道自己生命中最危險的兩年是出生那年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率還有退休那年
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道了他們的人生目標 , 也在他們的人生中活躍 , 值得大約七年多的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都小喝一口 , 卻不太會賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們往往以植物為主的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是大量的豆子和堅果
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來避免過量 , 一些小東西在適當的時間將它們推離餐桌 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 這一切的基礎是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一 , 照顧他們的孩子及年邁的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的族群 , 平均壽命四到十四歲之間 , 如果你一個月做四次的話 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的是 , 他們也屬於對的部落.
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就遇到對的人 , 就是主動把自己和對的人聚在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有50%的機率會變胖
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人混在一起 , 隨著時間的推移 , 那將會有很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友的休閒活動是體力活動 , 保齡球或打曲棍球、騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了點酒 , 但不過量他們吃得恰當 , 他們投入的信任和信任 , 信任和值得信任這會隨時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 歷史上 , 沒有飲食適用於超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始 , 通常都是在十月份完成 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽沒有短期的藥物或其他的功能
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你所能做的事當中 , 可能是最顯著的 , 能多增加年的生命 , 多到幾年的生命 。 非常感謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水導引電流 ; 一扇從清楚轉向不透明的窗口 ; 一扇製造音樂的果凍 。 一切都存在 。 卡塔琳娜•莫塔說:該是玩電玩的時候了 。 莫塔帶領我們一股驚奇和酷炫的新材料 , 並提醒我們 , 了解它們什麼是好的 , 去體驗 , 去體驗 , 去體驗 , 去體驗 , 去體驗 , 去體驗 , 去體驗和體驗 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧型材料玩耍
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機來建造車子 , 這樣他才能運送家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一個
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾有一段時間 , 我們了解事情如何運作 , 及如何制定 , 以便我們能建造和修復 , 或至少對購買的決定是有根據的 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在二十世紀的後半期 , 許多diy的做法都遺失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社區和開放原始碼模型正將東西的運作及其成分帶回我們的生活中而我相信我們需要將它們帶到下一個階段 , 帶到組成元件的材料上
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品等傳統原料是由什麼製成的 , 以及如何生產出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但是現在我們有這些令人驚嘆又有未來感的複合材料可以改變形狀 , 油漆可以導電 , 可以變換顏色的顏料 , 可以亮起來的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們可以畫電路 , 而不是用傳統印刷電路或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 藉由開啟這個小燈來感應我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家一直在用導電油墨 , 但近期的發展表示 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這塊丙烯酸纖維附滿了無色的散光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸纖維只會在邊緣散射光 , 這一片會在我開燈的時候散射整個表面 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這項材料有兩種已知的應用 , 包括內部設計以及多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱色素則會在特定溫度下改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	我把這個放在熱盤子上 , 它的溫度只比一般環境高一點點 , 看看會有什麼結果 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這項材料主要的應用是在嬰兒奶瓶上它能顯示內容物是否涼了可以喝了
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	以上只是一些普遍被稱為智慧型材料的例子
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年內 , 它們會以我們日常生活中常用到的許多物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說裡的飛行汽車但我們可以有能隨著溫度改變顏色的牆壁可以捲起來的鍵盤以及能在開關時不透明的窗戶
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一個社會科學家 , 藉由訓練 , 為什麼今天我要來這裡講智慧型材料呢 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造者 。
