i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何形成的 , 但也因為我相信我們應該有更深的認識這些構成我們世界的元件 , 而現在 , 我們對這些我們未來的高科技複合材料所知不足 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以在少量下取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	如何使用它們 , 幾乎沒有任何資訊可用 , 也幾乎沒有人知道它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們大多存在於這個貿易秘密和專利領域中 , 只有大學和企業能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年多前 , kirsty男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 " 開放材料 " 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是個網站 , 我們 , 以及任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人隨時都可以做出貢獻 , 並收集資源 , 如研究論文和教學 , 由其他和自己一樣的製造者所收集 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、集體生成的數據庫 , 由智能材料來自行生成 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但是為什麼我們要關心智慧型材料的運作以及組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解的東西和使用最後塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品、我們穿的衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在由智慧型材料組成的世界中 , 我們應該要知道且了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直是靠著tinker的力量推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘者 , 而不是專家 , 都是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學很複雜 , 且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但也不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學有兩位科學家了解到 , 當他們出版了一篇論文 , 用比較簡單的方法製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登邦克在讀論文前完全沒有相關化學經驗 , 只讀到這篇論文 , 並在自造者太空中重現了這個實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至根據其他科學家的說明書自製自己的旋渦混合器
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來將自己的成果公佈在網路上 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過、不成功的事情 , 讓其他人可以研究、複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬登創新的主要形式是把一個在大學設備精良的實驗室裡所做的實驗在他在芝加哥家中的車庫重新創造 , 只使用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己做出來 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項研究 , 其他人可以接觸到他離開的地方 , 甚至設計出更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個我想提及的例子是 , 她的專案計畫的目標是要強調材料的質量 , 同時要注重建造者的創造力和技巧 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 能教導我們東西的運作方式 , 但它們的設計與限制 , 會影響到我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的辦法是發想出一系列的技術來創造不尋常的物品讓我們不受限於預先設定的束縛藉由教導我們如何自行設計的材料
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗裡這是我最喜歡的一個
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅線 , 連到mp3播放器和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究 , 漢娜用許多不同的材料製作出一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布及墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像喬登以及許多其它的製造者 , 漢娜以她的食譜出版 , 讓任何人都可以複製、重製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學最前景的分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出較便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝成果 , 以及她分享了她的發現的事實 , 開啟了一連串美感吸引人和創新的門 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於我們用熱情和好奇心來創造 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常從不因循守舊的角度來處理問題 , 過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 甚至是更好的做法 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人在材料上做實驗 , 就有越多研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 我們就有更好的機會創造出真正能服務所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我有點像泰德.尼爾森在1970年代早期寫道: 「 你們現在一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是只有科學家在關心的大型主機 , 沒有人夢想要有一個人在家 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 有點奇怪 , 我現在站在這裡說: 「 你們現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 要取得新興科技的先進知識 , 是確保我們未來能有發言權的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖門 , 按下加速器 , 依靠我們的眼睛 , 來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面和後面的幾輛車 。 但如果汽車可以互相分享資料 , 分享它們的位置和速度 , 並使用預測模型來計算在路上給每個人最安全的路線呢 ? 珍妮佛•喜利想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛.喜利:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能可以避免意外發生 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不願去想的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 世界各地的宗教畫像和祝福畫上都出現在儀表板上 , 完全背道而馳的事實是我們知道的這個就是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲青年死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而當中75%與毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能確定 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是年輕的開車出去高速公路上 , 我前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我心想: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也慢了下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩著剎車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙不是減速的 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在停車 , 停車 , 在高速公路上停車 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	那時它只剩下65%到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs踢進去 , 那輛車仍舊繼續前進 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋佈署 , 車子全開 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車停了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 藉由讓車子彼此交流
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想讓你們稍微思考一下現在開車的經歷是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上你的車 。 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你就在這個延展型態的身體裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是 , 將它導航向部分路徑 , 及其他金屬巨人 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你是你的兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 這就是你們僅有的眼睛 , 不是真的為了這個任務而設計的 , 但接著 , 有人問你做這樣的事 , 你想要改變車道 , 他們第一個要你做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上移開 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看你前進的方向 , 轉彎 , 看你的盲點 , 然後不看你要往哪裡開 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	在座各位和其他人 。 這是安全駕駛的方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看這邊還是這邊 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作 , 選擇要走的路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們也會覺得有些不對勁或太晚了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機都說: 「 我沒看到它來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 , 我相信這點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看到這麼多
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現有的科技可以幫助我們改善這個狀況 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 車輛之間能互相交換資料 , 我們將能看到 , 不只三輛車在前面 , 後面三輛車在左邊 , 全都在同一時間 , 鳥瞰視野中 , 我們將能夠實際地看到車子內部 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們可以看到前面車輛的速度 , 可以看出前面車輛開得多快或停得多快 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人降到零 , 我會知道
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠預見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你們可能認為那不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你怎麼能預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不是 。 對車子而言 , 這不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車是立體的物體有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路往下走
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在有預先發表的路線上行駛 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來會去到哪裡並不困難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算你在你的車上 , 又來了摩托車 , 一小時85英里 , 車道簡化了--我知道你們一定有過這樣的經驗--那人可不是 " 無中生有 " 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在過去半個小時都在路上 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英里前 , 有人看見了那個傢伙 , 只要有一部車看到了那個傢伙 , 然後把他放在地圖上 , 他在地圖上 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英里的速度持續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他的車也會在他耳邊低語一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士等著看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測車子的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	那對他們很在行 。
so how do we get there ?	那我們該如何達到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 分享我們車子之間的位置資料 , 只是分享gps而已 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車上有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我對於我所在的位置以及我有多快的速度 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子位置 , 大概是 , 以及他們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以對自己所在的位置有著精準的認識 , 也有對其他車所在位置的模糊的概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車子共享那些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以精確的告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬結果 , 當估算結合時 , 會發生什麼事 , 甚至是輕浮的交通 , 當車子分享gps資訊 , 我們將這個研究從電腦模擬中移出 , 轉移到裝有實際感應器的機器人上 , 這些感應器裝置現在都在機械上:音響 , gps , 和二度雷射測距儀 , 都是用普通的備份發射器 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝上一台短距的無線電機 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人來到彼此身邊時 , 它們會精準地追蹤到彼此的位置 , 就可以避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合物中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你收到太多的章節 , 要處理所有的封包 , 就很難 , 所以你得要優先處理 , 而那是預測模型協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你就不會太注意那些封包 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先考慮一個傢伙 , 他看起來有點偏離常規 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	而你能預測出新的軌道
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道了 , 你還知道他要怎麼偏 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道哪個駕駛人需要提示警覺走出去 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做我們要如何警告每個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車要怎麼小聲警告: " 你得趕緊離開這裡 "
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這得靠兩件事:一 , 車子的性能二 , 駕駛能力
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上或者 , 你知道的 , 做一些事 , 他們可能不是最適合在緊急狀態下做出反應的 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始進行分離研究 , 做關於駕駛者狀態模型的研究 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	而現在 , 使用一系列的三相機 , 我們可以偵測到司機向前看、往外看、往手機看、或是喝一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預知事故我們可以預知是誰、哪一輛車子最佳的位置就出手去計算出每個人最安全的路線
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上這些科技在今日仍然存在
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為 , 我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是非常令人不安的觀念 , 認為我們的車子會在看著我們 , 和其他車子談我們 , 說我們會在一片流言蕭條的大海中走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用保護我們的隱私的方式來做到 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我不太清楚你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌號碼我不太清楚你是誰
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信 , 我們的車子可以在背後談論我們自己 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這將會是件很棒的事
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望各位花點時間想想 , 如果你真的不希望你們身後那些被分心的青少年知道你要煞車 , 你要停下來了 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們能做對每個人最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以讓你的車去聊吧 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	這將會讓道路變得更安全
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦者彼得.戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬霍金實現了他夢想的旅行 , 通過一起飛進大氣中 , 一起飛入大氣中 , 體驗無重力的程度 , 且不重量是無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	企業 , 飛行 , 科學 , 簡短的演講 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdiamandisstephenhawking在無gro的情況下
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我熱衷於打開太空門戶 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可思議的 。
and i want to tell you that story .	而我想要告訴你那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次認識他是在基因組學archonxprize的 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個能在十天內完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一個叫做 「 基因體一百 」 的個體 , 我們正在定序為其中一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特那次活動的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	然後我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你上去 , 但我能帶你進入無重力狀態 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對可以 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 在地球上 , 唯一可以體驗無重力的辦法 , 其實是用拋物線飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	帶上飛機 , 飛過頂點 , 25秒的無重力 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 體重有兩倍
you do it again and again .	你一而再、再而三的做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署對太空人進行這麼久的訓練 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算要做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要讓史蒂芬•霍金
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有個政府機關和一間公司的經營人說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你要殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	而他也想去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場記者會 , 我們宣佈我們打算要做一個無重力拋物線 , 給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼想上去做這件事
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命 , 總是有不斷增加的風險 , 可能會被災難所消滅......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對空間的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 前往nasa的車子裡 , 前往zero-g飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款我們募到了15萬美元作為兒童慈善機構的捐款 , 他們跟著我們一起飛 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾位ted會員
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整間急診室
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液中的po2值 , 他的心跳速率 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們所有的事情都發生在緊急情況 , 天知道 , 你並不想傷害這位世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭起飛 , 降落地面 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我的夥伴byronlichtenberg跟我小心地將他吊死在zerog 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他體驗無重力的真正樣貌 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	經過第一個拋物線飛行後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他笑了 , 我們就說去 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	實際上 , 我們讓一顆蘋果漂浮到艾薩克•牛頓爵士 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋大學擔任和艾薩克•牛頓相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四、第五、第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	以及第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個男人看起來不像是一個65歲的輪椅的人
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在一顆珍貴的珠寶上 , 我們的一生都在搬離這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們一同參與這場史詩般的探險
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫師大衛•鮑林斯基呈現了三分鐘令人驚艷的動畫 , 呈現出一個細胞內部的有趣生活 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化等
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插畫家 , 我的看法略有不同 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在關注 , 自從我長大 , 藝術中真與美的表現方式 , 以及科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都很美好 , 兩者都有非常美好的東西 , 能將它們──真與美──即是能被科學和數學所檢視的理想對象──幾乎就像是理想的連體雙胞胎──一個科學家會想要約會 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真實的表達方式 , 像是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的、不可救藥的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們獨特之處 。 它們有時也很有用 , 通常是之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在其實可以滾動一些照片了因為我不想在螢幕上看著我
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	對於不懂科學的人來說 , 真和美是不好的東西 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來描述美的事物 , 通常只有在你理解了這個主題的語言和詞彙中 , 才會描述真與美的事物 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有一個人類學的理想 , 在那裡 , 你看到生命必須由描述宇宙的數字進化而來 , 這些東西是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	從我作為一個醫學插圖師的經驗 , 到我從事一個動畫 , 是一個雕塑家 , 也是我的視覺導師--我想找出一種方法 , 幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美--透過動畫 , 通過使用圖片 , 訴說故事--這些不見得很明顯的事物可以被帶到人們身上 , 並且可以被教導 , 可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	今天的學生常常沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們所學的主題當中 , 有真與美的事物隱藏在其中 , 但他們被教導的方式是非凡的 , 並且被歸類到一個重點 , 在那裡 , 真與美並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是用來煮雞湯的古老食譜 , 直到香味不見了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生這麼做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue的電話 。 他問我我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫療與科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的計畫 , 這個計畫探討分子與細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 這樣一來 , 學生就能夠了解所有這些事實的一個更大的面貌 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以有一個心智圖像 , 把細胞當作一個大型、繁忙、極其複雜的城市 , 被微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械處於生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 讓世界各地充滿了奈米技術的羨慕 , 是自我引導、強大、精準、精確的裝置 , 這些都是由胺基酸鏈所組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械讓一個細胞如何移動 ,
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們可以供給細胞複製、供給我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們驅使我們的思想 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是想辦法把這個故事做成動畫將是哈佛大學biovisions主流製作的動畫 , 是一個哈佛大學為分子與細胞生物學學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有的文字資訊 , 把所有概念放在一起 , 這樣這些學生就有了體內的真與美 , 並且能夠透過這個觀點去研究 , 激發他們腦中的這些想像力和想像力 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 巨噬細胞會沿著微血管不斷移動 , 它們會觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從毛細管壁上獲取信息 , 它們會得到這些信息 , 這些信息會在外面某處產生發炎 , 看不到和感覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到資訊會使他們停下來 , 造成他們內化 , 他們需要製造出所有各式各樣的零件 , 能夠改變它們的形狀 , 並試著脫離這個微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家和數據庫模型一起合作 , 用原子上精確的分子模型 , 找出它們是如何移動 , 並且弄清楚它們是怎麼做的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	然後想辦法用真誠的方式來達成 , 讓它能呈現出發生的狀況 , 但卻不太真實 , 讓細胞中的隱密群眾得以避免發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	所以我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘讀者的最初版本我們製作的這個影片的最初版本 。 這是一個持續進行中的計畫 , 預計要進行四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們能看著這邊 , 看到細胞製造這些走路的小機械 , 它們被稱為 「 動作 」 , 能承受巨大的負荷 , 以相對大小的尺寸挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請跑這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動著細胞內部的機器真的是相當驚人的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此之間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們互相傳遞訊息
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們導致細胞內發生不同事情 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會真的在果蠅身上製造它所需的零件從讀取細胞核的資訊中 , 藉由讀取基因的分子來製造
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到今天在座的各位 , 如果沒有這些小微機械 , 就有可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 沒有這些機器的狀況下 , chris的出席率真的很低 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex快遞小伙子 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他拉著一個包裹 , 裡面滿是全新的製造蛋白質 , 到細胞所需的任何地方不論是到細胞膜、不管是到器官、不管是用來製造東西或修復某些東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這樣的東西在你一百兆個細胞中跑來跑去 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上 , 你其實什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	回家後 , 我希望各位能想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞多麼強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到的關於細胞機械學的一些事情 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了所有正在進行的而且相信我 , 我們幾乎都知道發生了什麼事的百分之一 , 一旦我們搞懂了正在發生什麼事 , 我們將能對我們健康、對未來世代所做的許多掌控 , 以及我們將活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能藉此發現更多真理 , 和更多美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但非常驚人的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 足以意識到細胞需要什麼它們來達到它們的目的 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們同心協力 。 它們使細胞做它該做的 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起努力 , 幫助我們的身體巨大的實體 , 那些他們永遠無法正確看見的實體 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	beckybrlanton計劃要在車上住一年 , 見識這個國家但是當憂鬱症出現時她的自由工作結束了她的露營旅行變成了無家可歸 。 在這場親密的演說中她描述她經歷到成為美國無家可歸的工作之一
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、故事等等 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:我那年是流浪漢
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 同時也是一個出於好奇的人 , 所以在22年的記者中 , 我學會了怎麼做很多新事情 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做的事情之一 , 就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年二月去世之後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這件事的時候 , 會有很多事情想要感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營我決定在旅行車上住一年就像一趟漫長的露營旅行
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	我帶著貓 , 我的rotweiler和露營裝備到1975年雪佛蘭旅行車上 , 開車前往日落 , 卻完全沒想到三件重要的事情 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會把活在永久的結構 , 甚至只是個小屋 , 作為一個人 , 都有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到 , 很快地 , 其他人的負面看法對我們的現實有多大的影響 , 如果我們放任它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	起初 , 住在旅行車裡很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃飯
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆、哀悼 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但之後因父親過世而感到憤怒和沮喪
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由性工作結束了 。 而我必須找全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來溫和的春天整個夏天都變成了一個極度炎熱的夏天
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在公園的任何地方 , 都不可能停車 , 很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 非常熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	那隻貓跑過了一個開窗的旅行車
the doggy went into doggy day care .	那隻狗走進白天護士
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	不論何時 , 我都用辦公大樓和卡車站的員工洗澡 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是在公共場所清理乾淨
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓人難以入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 ,
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰箱裡的冰塊在數小時之內融化了 , 那真是非常悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法買得起公寓 , 也無法買得起一間公寓 , 讓我能擁有圓頂小貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我留在旅行車中 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣使我無法走上50呎長的路到公共廁所在外的車子時晚上我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度下降到低溫狀態 , 然後停留在那裏 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對著一整套全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都把車子停在不同的地方 , 這樣我才能避免被警察發現和騷擾 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不是一直都很成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我無法控制我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道是何時 , 或如何發生 , 但我從一個才華橫溢的作家和記者 , 到一個無家可歸的女性 , 住在旅行車中 , 把我的呼吸抽了下來 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒變 , 我智商沒降
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的正直、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的一切 , 都不盡相同 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我某程度上改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪的旋渦裡越走越深
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人提名我去一間無家可歸的健康診所
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我就去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的人一樣沮喪、一樣沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	只是我沒喝醉 , 沒喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數不清的流浪漢意識到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸者 , 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人不認為我是無家可歸的人 , 但我還是一樣 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 ,
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 "
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的抗抑鬱藥有種反應讓我有自殺傾向 , 我記得當時心想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯塞特是一位國有名的記者 , 她一直在全國電視台上談到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	一篇我寫有關我父親的文章在他去世的前一年在提姆的新書
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在表演電路 , 而他正在談論我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到提姆•羅斯特《遇見傳媒前主持人》時 , 提姆•羅斯特談到我的寫作 , 當時我住在沃爾瑪停車場的休旅車裡 , 我開始大笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了 , 因為到頭來我是個作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 發現提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裏 , 重讀著我的文章
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回了田納西
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我住在休旅車和朋友家的沙發衝浪時 , 都在改變 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我擔任記者
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我是贏家 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 兼職工作 , 還住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化 , 犯罪化住在你的車上或街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸的人 , 主要還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到一位 , 讓他們投入 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給予他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服一切困難 , 如果它有了希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢給你們認識的下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 大家不是生活的地方、睡眠 , 或生活處境 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 永遠都能找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaida , 帶著我們走過全國大膽的計畫 , 去提升它的生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 而這代表著很多法蘭克 , 很好笑且非常有效的談論安全套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球性議題、健康、人口、科學
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	米奇雅:保險套先生如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人的時候 , 這個國家是非常非常貧窮的 , 有非常多的人生活在貧窮的環境裡 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或是從貧窮減碳計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但是我們從一個家庭照護計畫開始 , 跟著一個非常成功的孕產婦兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃如果他們的孩子沒有生存的話 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以第一步:先接觸兒童 , 先接觸母親 , 然後再接續家庭計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 1974年就是如此 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭平均有7個孩子 , 成長率達到3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 就做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: " 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來開藥 。 " 而且我們有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有採取不做為的答案 ; 我們沒有考慮到
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們找護士和助產士 , 她們也是女性 , 她們做了一份很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用避孕藥 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很美好 , 但整個國家只覆蓋了百分之二十 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們對其他80%的人做了些什麼 , 讓他們孤獨說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定要多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們就去看你看到的一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那個黃色的標誌下面--我希望他們沒有看過 , 因為當時有可口可樂 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	我們當時比可口可樂高得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的對象是我們選的對象 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區內很有名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己做家事規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供避孕藥品和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	就這樣 , 我們去找那些被視為問題的原因來解決問題的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 你都能看到船上載著婦女 , 賣東西是漂浮市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找到人 , 你都會找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 何不去宗教因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會相當堅強 , 泰國人都是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 聽著 , 你們能幫我們嗎 ? 」

in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮苦人家來說 , 鑽石不會使得它變成--所以保險套是女孩的最好朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年介紹了我們第一個小額貸款計畫 , 其中有組織的女性說: 「 我們只想借給實行家庭計畫的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果妳懷孕了 , 照顧妳的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們這裡貸款 。 」

and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年 , 還在持續進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 不是真的銀行 , 而是基金的微型貸款 。

then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病襲擊泰國 , 我們得要停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。

these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三、四年級 , 要到村子裡的每一個家庭、整個泰國的家庭 , 給予艾滋病資訊和保險套給每一個家庭 , 由這些孩子提供 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人民脫離貧窮 , 現在我們用愛滋病的方式 , 這次不只和政府單獨合作 , 也和商業社群合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 也缺乏信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些都是商業社群能提供的東西 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著要把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法是透過企業企業企業
so , that was done .	完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	資金從公司進入村落 , 移植樹木 。
it's not a free gift .	這可不是免費的禮物

and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在借錢前 , 你需要先接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想要幫助貧窮的人 , 那些生活在貧窮之中的人 , 信用能力一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用能力必須要成為人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠脫離不了貧困 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	接著 , 在取得貸款之前 , 你必須要先接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	以下是我們所稱的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 如此一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 就會成功做生意 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 終於 , 在教育上 , 我們希望改變學校的做法 , 讓學校被當做一個終身學習中心 , 供所有人使用 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會覺得是朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你微笑一陣子 。 在ted2013年 , 凱拉多•雷娜•德摩斯羅摩 , 智慧手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 它們可以隨時隨地陪伴你 , 滑走一杯咖啡然後用可程式化的表情回應你 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人為你的手機供電 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉一下手你們中有多少人家中都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	沒幾個人 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們romotive公司想解決的問題 , 我和其他20位宅男在romotive做的 , 他們很著迷於解決 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要打造一個任何人都可以用的機器人不管你是八歲還是八十歲
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這真的是個困難的問題 , 因為你必須打造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不僅僅是真正負擔得起 , 它還必須是人們真正想要帶回家的東西 , 並帶著孩子回家 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人無法令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo這個機器人 , 使用一種你已經知道且喜愛你的iphone作為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造一個有wifi功能的機器人 , 並且擁有電腦視覺能力 , 大約有150塊美金 , 這大約是這類型的機器人在過去會花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是用設備上攝影機來跟蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我躲下 , 他會跟著我走 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很疑惑 , 所以他會把目光放在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我到這邊 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他會感到害怕 , 就像任何生物一樣 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	在很多方面 , romo像是一隻有自己想法的寵物 。

and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就跟你在ipad上滑動頁面的方式一樣 , 我實際上可以調整裝置上攝影機的角度 。

but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo最重要的事是我們想要創造一個完全依靠直覺的東西 。
