but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常非常令人驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會看到你鼻子中大約百分之二十的基因信息不符合任何我們以前曾經見過的東西--沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對我們這些實際在研究這種資料的小團體而言 , 其實我們當中少數人已經開始稱這個資訊為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何以前我們看過的東西 ; 它有點像是我們基因信息中一塊未知大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻腔中百分之20的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達百分之40或50的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約1% ~ 2%的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法被我們以前見過的任何東西歸類或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為也許這是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對更新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這些信息是一種生命型態 , 至少有一部分是生命型態 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設其實只是在其嬰兒期 , 有一個非常非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那埋藏在生命中 , 在這個遺傳信息中 , 是還未被辨識出來的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c、g , 我們可能會揭開一個全新的生命階段 , 就像beijerinck一樣 , 從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這也許能讓我們找出折磨人類的癌症病源 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的爆發病症病源體 , 或也許能創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興的宣布 , 同時加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們 , 我們正在開始一項計畫 , 要探索生物暗物質 , 針對新形式的生命存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們都不知道病毒 , 一種組成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形態 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們會驚嘆我們可能完全不知道有新種類的生命存在 , 就在我們的鼻子裡 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能發現了所有在那裡的哺乳類動物 , 但這不代表地球上沒有剩下什麼可以探索的 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同伴提供了一個重要的課題給下一代的探險家就像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩一樣
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們把這個教訓說成是這樣的話:不要假設我們目前認為有的就是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求任何你選擇要探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都有未知的事物 , 它們等待著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說大衛.迪奇在後台放了理論物理 , 來討論更急迫的問題:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在我們在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出一個肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這麼做 , 但我想先從大家都知道的兩件事說起 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	而第一個 , 事實上 , 是有史以來最為人所知的東西 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是 , 地球 , 或太陽系 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境等等 , 都被獨特適合用來維持我們的演化或創造 , 正如它過去的思想、現在的存在 , 以及最重要的 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	今天這個想法有個很戲劇化的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 內在是一切的 , 我們賴以為生的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們弄亂我們的太空船 , 我們沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 第二件大家都知道的事 , 與我們所相信的人類歷史大多相反 , 人類事實上並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如stephenhawking所說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面上的化學污垢 , 它就在一個典型的恆星旁邊 , 它位在一個典型的銀河系的邊緣 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	現在 , 大家都知道的第一件事 , 有點像是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨特適合 , 等等 。 第二件事是說我們處在一個很典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是當你把這兩件事當作生命中深刻的真理並以此作為你人生決策的依據 , 那麼他們似乎彼此有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止兩者都是完全錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的地方開始 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們環顧四周 , 看看四周 , 看向一個隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 還有一個化學污垢 , 那完全不是宇宙的典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要朝著同一個方向前進幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看見任何牆壁或化學污垢 , 你只會看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走的更遠 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不是宇宙中典型的現象因為恆星存在於星系中
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 離任何銀河系都很近 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們走出銀河 , 再往回看 , 是的 , 巨大的星系在我們面前展開 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時我們已經走了十萬光年
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們還沒有接近宇宙中一個典型的地方.
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你要到達星系間空間的1000倍以上 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	以極高的代價來說 , ted已經安排了一種高清晰度的 「 沉浸式虛擬實境 」 , 利用星系間空間來呈現 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 看得見嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你看到在星系間空間是完全黑暗的 , 陰暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正看著離你最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星正如超新星般爆炸 , 當光線射到你的時候 , 你甚至會無法看到甚至閃爍的光芒 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙是多大又黑暗
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的光亮 , 令人讚嘆的一個事件 , 它會讓你在幾光年內結石死亡 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你根本看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷絕對零度不到三度
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它非常空曠 。 真空的密度比目前地球上最好的科技能創造的真空量少了一百萬倍 。 這是從這個地方來的截然不同 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這地方就是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	拜託 , 我們能開燈嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道這麼遠的一個環境 , 如此不同 , 如此不同 , 如此不同於我們習慣的任何事物 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式存在--創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 看遠一點看 , 我是說從這裡開始 , 用望遠鏡--你會看到類似恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 類星體 」 。 原本的 「 類星體 」 指的是 「 類星體 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	也就是說 , 看起來有點像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	而我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 甚至數十億光年之遙 , 一個星系中心的物質朝著一個超大質量的黑洞塌陷.
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後密集的磁場引導了一些重力塌陷的能量 。 其中的一些物質 , 以巨大的噴流的形式回到外面 , 照亮了一兆個地球 , 我認為是太陽的光亮 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理幾乎不像這樣噴射流的物理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在其中一個噴射流中存活下來 。 語言在其中一個噴流中斷裂 , 無法形容當時的情況 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像經歷一次超級新星爆炸 , 但一次是零距離 , 數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射流發生得如此地精確 , 以至於數十億年後在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 和預測 , 並且解釋 , 最重要的是你參考了那裡正在發生的事情 , 在現實中 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	其中一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了一個 「 另一個 」 的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅只是一個表面的圖像 , 雖然它包含了那個圖像 , 也包含了解釋性的模型 , 具體呈現出同樣的數學關係 , 同樣的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 , 如果這還不夠驚人 , 對另一種結構的信心會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有著這種特殊的特性 ,
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物件 , 不像它們可能的樣子 , 除非它們能夠體現出同樣的數學和因果結構 , 且隨著時間的推移 , 進行的越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含不斷的精密 , 所有東西的結構 。 這個地方 , 和宇宙中的其他地方 , 是一個包含一切結構和因果關係的樞紐 , 包含整個實體現實的結構和因果關係 。 至今 , 物理定律允許這一切發生 , 甚至是強制性的 , 是實體世界最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們之中的形式是如何取得這種與宇宙其他部分特殊的關係的呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金的評論中 , 有一件事是對的 , 但強調的確是錯的 。 有一件事是對的 , 不是用任何特殊的物理學來實現的 。 沒有特殊的憑證 , 沒有奇蹟的憑證 。 它只用了三件我們豐富的事物來實踐 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊的處理是計算 , 電腦需要的是沒有物質的知識 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠影響我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放式的知識、解釋 , 也是必要的 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境中充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好在測試的時候 , 比如說 , 牛頓的萬有引力定律大約在300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去的證據 , 早在那之前 , 就落在地球上的每平方公尺上 , 數十億年後 , 還會持續下去 , 數十億年後 , 其他的科學也一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學最基本真理的證據就在我們的星球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也伴隨著物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三項開放式的知識創造 , 都要從它們的可能性中做到最低 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 外面一片漆黑 , 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實這只是另一個狹隘的錯誤觀念 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像一個在星系間空間中的立方體 , 跟我們的家大小一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體被人類的標準給空了 , 但仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造 , 比方說 , 一個自給自足的太空站 , 裡面有一群科學家 , 致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 遠遠超出現今的科技甚至把來自星系間空間的氫氣收集起來 , 形成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果有東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼事可能可以阻止我們這麼做 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識 , 而不是資源的問題 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動做到這點 , 就有能源供應 , 因為變異會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片.但是你要做的 , 就是拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是現在設計 , 向外看--你會看到和我們這裡一模一樣的星系.
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	再加上一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看到恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠做到天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地你可以建造粒子加速器 , 並且學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等.
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能到達最近的有生命存在的星球 , 再回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起richard--但是我從來都不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔數億年才進行一次.
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間包含了所有開放式的知識 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何地方 , 都可以成為和我們一樣的中心 , 只要我們知道怎樣做 , 都能在當下存在 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是唯一適宜居住的地方
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠創造出一串開放式的解釋 , 那麼 , 幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 地球也是一樣 。 受污染的地球也是一樣 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 但知識 , 很匱乏 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以知識為基礎的宇宙觀也許--而我認為應該讓我們感覺到十分特殊 。 但同時也應該要讓我們感覺到脆弱 , 因為這意味著如果沒有特定的知識在宇宙中存活下去的那些挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星 , 我們都會死 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯 , 最重要的是用大規模毀滅性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率能在這個世紀存活 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他以後會在會議上談到這點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我的確同意他的看法 。 我們能生存 , 無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於偶然 , 而是我們是否能及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並非完全是前所未見的 。 物種隨時會滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終究會結束 。 絕大多數曾經存在過的物種和所有的文明都是現在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用這個特徵來區別我們這個物種 , 以及我們的文明 , 從所有其他人而來的 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋的能力 , 新知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這件事用在當前的一個爭議上 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來說明我所指的那類問題 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 。 說到全球暖化 , 我只是個懶惰的人 。 做法是認真看待先前的科學理論 。 根據理論 , 已經太遲了 , 無法避免任何災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果目前我們最好的選擇是用一種像是京都議定書之類的 , 來防止二氧化碳排放 , 它的經濟活動限制非常大 , 花費數百億美元之類的 , 那麼任何合理的措施都已經是一場災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	所提倡的行動 , 甚至沒有為解決問題而爭取 , 僅僅是稍微推遲這個問題 。 所以 , 為了避免它已經太遲了 , 而且從有人意識到危險之前 , 可能已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能在1970年代時就已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放即將推動一個新的冰河時期 , 數十億人會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這堂課讓我很清楚 , 我也不知道為什麼它沒有告知公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能一直都知道 。 當我們知道一個即將發生的災難 , 以及如何以低於災難本身的成本來解決 , 那麼其實不會有太多爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 就可以避免我們還不曾預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的辦法 , 不只是問題的解決 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防等於一磅一盎司的解藥 , 但前提是我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你因為鼻子被打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學就不會教你如何避開拳頭 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治愈 , 只專注於預防 , 那麼它也幾乎不會達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此刻世界正掙扎著計畫去強迫氣體排放不計成本的減量
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要和計畫配合降低溫度的計畫 , 計畫要在更高溫度下生存 , 且不是不計成本 , 而是有效地、便宜地生活 。 還有一些計畫存在 , 像是在太空中放置鏡子 , 來將太陽光反射出去 , 並鼓勵水生生物吃更多二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類投入心力去面對這個問題的中心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	面對的問題 , 我們還未意識到 , 放棄權利的能力 , 不是無限期的躲避幸運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 更是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩塊石板 , 然後在上面刻上雕刻 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一張雕刻上寫著: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果困在不良規則的體制 , 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭露了一個很大膽的想法: 「 特區市 」 , 城市管理區被聯盟所統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅羅默的激進想法:特區市 。
take a look at this picture .	請看一下這張照片
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它有個非常引人注目的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	現在 , 我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我碰過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 選一張吧 , 穿綠色衣服的人
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	咱們也來給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢說尼爾森有支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以謎題來了:
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以接觸到像手機這樣尖端的科技 , 但卻無法接觸到一百年來在家中產生電燈的科技 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案就是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以防止雙贏解決方案可以實現 , 只要有人能把新技術帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人也能用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司按照規定來運作 , 也就是說 , 它必須以極低的電費補貼來銷售 , 事實上 , 它的電費非常低 , 低到每賣一單位都要損失經費 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去幫很多用戶接種 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到了 , 不同規則的存在是有可能的 , 企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有動機去簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是尼爾森公司購買的手機業務規則 , 由尼爾森撥款公司來支付他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過那些規則是如何運作良好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他嘗試改變用電價制定的規則 , 但卻引發了一場抗議 , 抗議來自企業和消費者想要保存既有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困在規則中 , 以防他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森被困在街燈下做研究 ,
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	那時候真正的挑戰是 , 試著找出我們能如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則可以發展成用來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 我們有一個一般性的抽象洞見 , 可以實踐 , 那就是 , 如果我們可以給人們更多選擇 , 並且給那些在許多國家裡 , 領導者更多的選擇 , 他們也是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但是 , 要呈現出這兩者之間的反對意見是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者什麼樣的選擇 , 比如給總統一個選擇 , 提高電價的選擇 , 奪去經濟想要的人想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能繼續消耗補貼電力的選擇
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給兩者更多的選擇 , 那將會給我們一組規則 , 用來改變規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也有網路用 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞性影響 , 規則能讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署在夜間所拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡的輪廓 , 跟它的鄰居比起來 , 它就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們留在黑暗中
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是 , 要了解北韓和南韓開始時用的是同一套規則在法律和法規方面 , 在更深層的層面上 , 也要了解到 , 標準、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做出了選擇 , 導致了非常不同的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	因此 , 我們可以改變人類可以改變彼此互動的規則 , 無論是好事還是壞事 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 放大到這裡
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗相較於它的鄰居多明尼加共和國也差不多數量的居民
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相對於波多黎各來說 , 兩個國家都是暗的 , 這兩個國家都有半數的居民 , 不論是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們規則可能會很不好 , 因為政府很軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不僅僅因為政府實在太強勢與壓迫性 , 就像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有良好規則的環境 , 我們不能只撕下 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找出方法來建立
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示了與規則合作的潛力與挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料表的一開始 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人早已擁有像煉鋼、印刷、火藥等先鋒般的科技 ,
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則來鼓勵這些想法的傳播 , 一個有利潤的動機 , 可以促使它們傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快採用了一些規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 讓中國遠離世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 如同世界上其他國家創新 , 在這兩方面開發出更新的技術 , 但也發展出更新的規則 , 中國人卻因此失去了這些進步 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	國民所得停滯不前 , 世界其他國家都停滯不前 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了所得 , 中國平均所得佔美國平均所得的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到這個數字大約是3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代後期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的成長起飛中國人開始迎頭趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回看地圖 , 就可以知道這個過程會導致中國發生戲劇性的改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點是你在輪廓邊緣可以看到的 , 就是香港
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都處在一套截然不同規則的底下 , 和其他當時的中國規則 , 大體上 , 被當時的市場經濟所複製 , 和英國人管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有上百萬人能夠去的地方 , 從大地到大地 , 到從工作開始 , 像是縫衣、做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了取得增進收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致了當地的成長非常快速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個範例 , 領導人如鄧小平可以複製的模範 , 當他們決定全面推動整個大陸 , 進入市場經濟模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個中國人立即轉型到市場模式上 , 他們採取的方式是創建一些特區 , 在某種意義上 , 可以做到 , 只要英國做到:讓機會與願意參與的市場規則連接到想要選擇的人 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們創立了四個特別的經濟區 , 圍繞香港周圍:中國人可以到那兒工作的地方 , 城市迅速成長 ; 還有外國公司可以到那裏來 , 製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個地方有一個城市叫深圳
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一間台灣公司 , 在座很多人製作的iphone , 他們用來自中國的勞工製作的 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸區也在同一方面打開了 , 最後在這些地方展現出成功 , 讓人們能夠選擇去那裡 , 他們聚在一起 , 因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡展示成功帶來了共識 , 讓它朝向市場經濟模式前進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在的中國例子顯示了好幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:保留人民選擇的權利
two: operate on the right scale .	二:運作在對的尺度上 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你嘗試改變一個村落的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但是村落會變得太小到無法得到好處 , 如果你有數百萬人在有良好體制下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家過於大 ,
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你嘗試改變這個國家的規則 , 你不能給某些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 然後讓他人放大 , 嘗試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你這個機會 , 可以創造新的地方 , 只要有新的規則 , 大家就能夠選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	當數百萬人在有良好規則下 , 他們就已經夠大了 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以提議是我們對所謂 " 特區市 " 的概念
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一份特許書開始 , 針對所有規則所需的規則 , 來吸引建造這個城市所需要的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者這些人將建造基礎建設--電力系統 , 道路 , 港口 , 機場 , 建築
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司來 , 該公司會先僱用移入的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	而且你會需要吸引家家戶戶戶這些居民將會永遠的到來並住在那裡 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著那個憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡
the city can be built .	這座城市可以建造
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再 , 再而三地
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了使它可行 , 我們需要良好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中被捕捉到
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這已建構在模型中 , 如果我們能夠在沒有人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人的領土開始 ,
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的憲章底下生存 , 但沒有人是被逼著活下去的 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者選擇
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們期望的那種選擇我們需要在各國之間共同合作的可能性:讓各國一起合作的案件 , 實際上 , deo , 中國和英國同心協力建設的案例 , 先是小小的市場經濟模式 , 然後再擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國不經意地透過它在香港所做的行為 , 減少了世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫加起來還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這種合作方式再複製一次 , 我們就能得到全世界這麼大的利益 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這將涉及到一份責任的授權 , 一份控制權 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的授權 , 去監督某些管理職責 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我這樣說時 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 這是否只是帶回殖民主義 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	它不是 。 但很重要的是 , 要體認當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的那種情緒 , 可以讓我們倒退 , 可以讓我們倒退 , 關閉我們的能力 , 以及我們試圖探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方 , 在我們一些援助計畫中 , 反而不好的事情 , 就是它涉及了強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇的 , 無論是對領袖 , 還是對那些將住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是強制執行和執行的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何實踐它 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們以特別的領袖 , raulcastro為例 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定也想過他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做到的事情不過他並沒有香港在古巴這裡
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過他還是在南部留了點光 , 那裡有非常特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一區 , 在那裡有條約給予美國政府負責為一塊土地差不多是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大總理對他說: 「 瞧 , yankees有個可怕的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要脫身 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你們加拿大何不接手呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	打造一個特殊的管理區
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一座新城市建設在那裡
allow many people to come in .	允許許多人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近能有一個香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會保持住 。 但這就是通往我國家的現代經濟和現代世界的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模式還能在哪裡被試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我曾和領導人談過
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們之中很多人完全懂得特殊區塊的概念 , 人們可以選擇以此做為規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	制定改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人民在沒有強制的情況下做出 " 民意 " , 強制性 " 可以 " 反對力量 " 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下他們能對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾──那些投資者會來建港口、建造道路 , 在一個新的城市裡 , 他們能做出更有保障的承諾 , 只要他們能和一個合夥的國家合作 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某種安排中有點像是信託管理帳戶 , 把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡 , 合夥的國家需要為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多的土地可以建造新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這張照片是我在沿著海岸飛行時照的
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這片大地一樣有著巨大的延伸 , 能讓數億人居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納並思考不只是一兩個特區市 , 還有數十個城市 , 能為數億人創造居所 , 也許下個世紀就會有數十億人搬到城市去 , 會有足夠的土地容納他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界 , 如果我們在夜晚去看燈光 , 有一件事是誤導了 , 那就是 , 視覺上說 , 世界好像大部分都已經建造完成了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我來說明為什麼這樣做是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有的土地
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個正方形代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被三十億人居住的城市所消耗的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把圓點向下移到這個長方形的底部你會發現 , 對於現有的三十億城市居民的城市只佔了地球上百分之三的可耕地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們要為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們會是像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從百分之三的可耕地提升到百分之四
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大地減少人類在地球上的足跡 , 通過建造更多可以遷移的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是受良好體制管理的城市 , 他們可以是讓人安全的城市 , 不受犯罪、疾病和衛生不良的限制 , 人人都有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們能取得基礎設施 , 像是電力 ,
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一座特區的城市 , 要花什麼代價 , 才能建造更多呢 ?
it would help to have a manual .	這有助於使用手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們能做的就是寫些細節 , 可能進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者們走出野外 ,
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設不只加拿大會和卡斯楚有關係 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也參一腳西班牙 , 也許古巴想成為四向關節的合作夥伴之一
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何訂定條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有先例可循 , 但那很容易就能解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這件事 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	其實 , 新加坡和香港是一座針對自己剛開始所擁有土地所獲得的巨大城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的收入來支付如警察、法院等費用 , 但學校體制和健康照護體制 , 這也是一個更吸引人的地方 , 讓這個地方的居民能有更高的收入 , 如此一來 , 土地就更有價值了 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 激勵人們去幫助設立這個區塊並建立起它 , 並設立基本規則 , 往對的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有其他很多像這樣的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能有低成本、負擔得起的建築 , 給第一份工作的人打造像iphone一樣的東西 , 卻能讓那些建築物更有效率 , 並且確保它們是安全的 , 不會因為地震或是颶風而倒下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節要想出辦法 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些事的人 , 已經可以知道 , 沒有道路 , 沒有阻礙 , 除了一個失敗的想像力之外 , 還會阻礙我們去實現真正的全球性的雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片作結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以如此幸福 , 儘管地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以跟別人分享想法 , 當他們發現想法時 , 他們也會跟我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享的意義是我們每個人的收穫變少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那樣的方式來思考想法 , 我們通常會以科技的角度來思考 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類的想法:規則規則規則規則規則 , 規則像是:讓我們訂個賦稅制 , 來支撐一個研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們設立一個體制 , 在那裡我們擁有擁有土地在政府辦公室裡的所有權 , 人民可以隨心所欲地承諾 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷在制度上創新特別是在我們想出一些規則來改變規則所以我們不會卡在不良的規則上那麼我們就能繼續進步真正讓世界變得更好讓像尼爾森和他的朋友們再也不用在街燈下讀書了謝
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學先鋒們克萊格•凡特在史詩般的遠征中 , 需要一段時間 , 來談談他的團隊所發現的數百萬基因 , 目前為止 , 他的團隊在探索海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科學、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特對dna和海的研究 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	演講開始前 , 我被幾個人問到我對於老化辯論的看法 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將是我對它唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀的人比悲觀者要活得更長久 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在這18分鐘內要告訴你們的 , 就是我們將如何從讀取基因編碼轉換到開始自己編寫基因編碼的第一個階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前這個月我們公佈了第一批免費增生有機體的序列包含了嗜血桿菌流感
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	花了13年到4個月進行基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年裡 , 大量的基因組被加上了:大多數的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類的基因組 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	從十多年前開始 , 基因組學就在今年底 , 我們可能已經完成了三到五組基因組的測序 , 大約是幾百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	今年我們得到了 「 戈登與貝蒂摩爾基金會 」 資助 , 用來排序130組基因組 , 做為環境有機體的副產品 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因編碼的速率就改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有劃過這個星球上可看到的東西的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人沒有意識到它 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球一半的生物量 , 而所有的動物只佔了所有生物量的千分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許 , 牛津人不常做這種事 , 但如果你曾去過海邊 , 吞了一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中都有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	少於5 , 000種微生物物種被特徵為兩年前的特徵 , 所以我們決定採取行動 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了srceri的遠征隊伍 , 我們在那裡進行了很棒的海洋考察 , 嘗試著每隔200英里進行一次採樣 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始做測試計畫 , 接著移居到哈利法克斯 , 在美國東海岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 通過加拉巴哥群島 , 然後橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫越印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上進行此項任務 , 有部分能協助熱衷的年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是拿海水來過濾 , 然後在不同的濾嘴上搜集不同大小的生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時可以對一億個字母進行基因編碼的測序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	通過這樣做 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 當時認為我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一兩種有機體擁有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界上幾乎所有海上生物 , 在溫暖的部分 , 都有這些相同的光感接收器 , 並將陽光當作它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬種新基因和多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經將這個計畫延伸到空中 , 用來自史隆基金會的資助來實現 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量我們所有人每天呼吸多少種病毒和細菌 , 特別是在飛機或封閉的會堂裡 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們用一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們只用一天的時間 , 就收集到十億微生物的數量 , 在紐約市的大樓上過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	目前我們正在對這些做排序 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在收集資料的這一邊 , 我們透過加拉帕戈斯群島 , 發現幾乎每兩百英里 , 我們在海裡的樣本中就有非常大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些合理的說法是 , 不同溫度差異的指標 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張以溫度為基礎的衛星照片-紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水取樣與冰冷的水取樣有著極大的差異 , 以豐富的物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人驚訝的事是這些色素感光器探測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些不同區域的差異非常大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海中 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光受體通常會看見藍色的光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 他們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們有更大的變化 , 可能在極端的情況下 , 朝紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因庫的量 , 我們組裝了所有資料 , 包括所有我們遠離考察的數據 , 總數超過地球上半數的基因資料 , 總數約有2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家族看看這些發現是甚麼:我們是發現已知家庭的新成員嗎 ? 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但我們在環境中取得的每一個新樣本 , 都會針對這些新族群加以排列 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	因此 , 我們正處於發現基礎基因、組成物、生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物在右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	那些大約有2千9百萬個基因 , 我們的基因組中只有大約2萬4千種 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物放在一起看 , 我們大概不到三萬種 , 可能只有十幾種或更多的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅是演化的設計組成 ,
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們從基因中心論來看-也許回到了理查•道金斯的想法 , 而不是以基因組中心論來看 , 這些基因組成不同組成的構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 即dna合成的能力 , 已經改變的速度和dna測序的速度差不多 , 近二十年來 , 已經變得非常快速且非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對合成基因組的第一個想法是當我們在1995年做第二組基因組測序時 , 當時是從印尼生殖器取得的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800對基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題:如果某物種需要800組 , 另一組500組 , 是否有一組比較小的基因 , 可能構成最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子斷裂 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨機插入基因編碼的小段的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	而如果它們插入基因的中間 , 干擾它的功能 ,
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張所有可以接受轉位子插入的基因的地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現環境對此是非常重要的 , 你只能根據環境中的東西來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試採用更直接的方法 , 研究出13種相似有機物的基因組 , 我們試圖比較所有這些 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的迴圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173種基因具有全部13種生物的共通性 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了某顆細胞寄生蟲 , 水池會稍微擴張一點點 , 大約310組核心基因會更長 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為 , 我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 取決於你在這裡的觀點 , 將近300到400個基因 , 從最少500個基因開始 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要實現這些想法的唯一方法就是製造一條人工染色體 , 裡面有這些基因 , 我們必須在培養基礎的流程上做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片碎片中合成出正確的dna是極度困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 與我同事開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 達到100%準確度 , 以它的序列和生物學來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個相當令人振奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子轉過身然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這並不是第一種合成病毒-小兒麻痺病毒-已經在一年之前被製造出來 , 但只有原病毒1/100的活性病毒-要花三年才被製造出來 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的卡通結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這種情況下軟體會建立自己的硬體 , 那就是我們與生物學相關的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	大家立刻轉而關注生物戰 , 我最近在參議院委員會舉行前發表了證詞 , 美國政府設立了一個專門委員會來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 很重要的是要讓現實記住 , 與其讓人們的想像力有所不同 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經完成測序的病毒 , 都可以製造出該基因組 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	大家立刻對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐萬分 , 但這個有機體的dna沒有感染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心安全部門的問題是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯兩國 , 他們在試圖創造生物武器時 , 才投入大量心力 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那個研究真的被終止了 , 將來在製造製造設計師的病毒上應該不會有很少的動機 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 在兩年內 , 單細胞生物就有可能
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	很有可能在十年內 , 那些我們有著可能變成可能的真皮細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製作數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變培養皿和基因 , 進入到這個人造染色體中 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 如何將所有其他的
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組的系統 , 將這些片段重新組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , deinocococococcusradiodurans , 它可以承受三百萬拉德輻射而且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發過後它會在12至24小時內重組它的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上普遍存在 , 甚至可能因為我們在外太空的旅行而存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是由大約50萬拉德輻射照射過後的酒杯 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始發燒 , 發出啪聲 , 底部的微生物越來越快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際狀況的照片上方顯示的是經過170萬拉德輻射照射的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被完全粉碎了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是24小時後 , 同樣的dna自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的很令人吃驚 , 這些生物能夠做到這件事 , 我們在這個星球上可能有成千上萬 , 甚至上千種不同的物種能夠做到這件事 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成後 , 第一步就是將它們移植進一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 同時也為了期待環境和社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所測序的第三種生物上 , 甲烷janococcusjanaschii , 它生存在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫原子 , 它所有的碳元素都來自於二氧化碳--它從周圍環境中捕捉回來 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 數千種不同的生物以二氧化碳為生 , 可以將它捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從使用從石油中取得的來進行合成的過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 並從大氣中把碳捕回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體 , 住在一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來當作減少能量來分解水來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有無數的途徑 , 都可以透過改良代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦正在和挪威石油公司合作一項重大的計畫 , 要把來自天然氣田的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在不久的將來 , 我認為將會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些大量的基因定位複製以及同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 讓每天製造一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 正如所有生物學一樣 , 透過篩選來進行篩選 , 不管你是在篩選產生氫氣或化學生產 , 或僅是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因在其中扮演的角色 , 將會很好的接觸到 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用的過程 , 以直接從陽光照射產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的催化酶將會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞酶 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖類的酵素 , 並在同一個細胞裡發酵來製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	用微生物進行製藥生產已經在主要實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物化學作用的順序比我們最好的化學家能製造的還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來工程的物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 也許還能取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策的研究來作結 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審核是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與了這個
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	其實這是一個非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都在使用他們的經文作為法律書籍 , 卻找不到任何禁止創造生命的東西 。 所以 , 這真的很不錯 。 唯一的顧慮是生物戰的方面 , 但給了我們一些開始進行這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前史隆基金會剛資助一個多機構的研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和益處 , 以及像是我自己的科學團隊 , 應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 我們正在嘗試設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了對生物恐怖主義的威脅以外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們是否能設計東西來產生清潔能源 , 也許改革開發中國家的做法 , 並透過各種簡單的過程來提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲力普津巴多說 , 快樂和成功來自一個我們大部分人都不在乎的特質:我們朝向過去、現在和未來的方向前進 。 他建議我們用時間校正自己的前景 , 將我們改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心、心理學、科學
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo會開立一個健康的 「 準時 」 會議
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 在很短的時間內 ,
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	視頻:好 , 開始計時 , 三十秒 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間差不多 , 終結排序 , 拿一個

philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•津巴多:咱們來看看亞當的誘惑性成就 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 別那麼爽脆 , 咬一口 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 別棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 ,
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口 , 那要幹嘛 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑人的 。 這一切是為了產生、抵抗 , 是的 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 以後 , 衝動 , 反思 , 現在和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	被應許的美德跌到了當下的激情之中
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要宣誓要在婚前 , 實施性傾向和貞潔的少女 , 多虧了大多數 , 喬治布希 , 約60% , 會在一年內達到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	而他們中的大多數都沒有用節育能力 。
so much for promises .	多麼為了承諾啊 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以擁有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們會有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 就得等 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子用於誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 延後推
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米舍爾 , 我斯坦福大學的同事 , 14年後 , 嘗試去發現那些孩子有何不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在很多方面 , 抗拒的孩子和被量產的孩子之間有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抵抗sat考試的孩子 , 成績提高250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那是非常巨大的 。 那就像是一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上太多麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們有自信和決心 。 而對我來說 , 最重要的是 , 他們是 「 未來 」 , 而不是 「 現在式 」 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	觀點的研究是 , 針對個人 , 我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動 , 分成時間區域或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動和不自覺地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們會在文化、國家、個人、社會階級之間有差異 , 教育程度也不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們可能會有偏見 , 因為你學會了過度使用其中一些而其他的不當使用 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做出的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做出決定 , 你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在即時的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 你感覺如何 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們以那種形式作決策時──我們稱他們為 「 呈現 」 , 因為他們的焦點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在並不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 " 我在過去所經歷的這種情況是什麼 ? "
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的回憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們要稱這些人為 " 過去式 " , 因為他們關注的是過去式 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人而言--這不是過去式 , 也不是現在式 , 只針對未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們的重點在於將來會變成什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	因此 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是 , 時間觀念的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一個決策 , 你是完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有一種偏頗的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實 , 共有六種方式 , 有兩種方式可以用在現代 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以持久懷舊 , 兩種方式可以是未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以注重 " 正面懷舊 " 或 " 負面懷舊 "
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是現代主義的 , 也就是你把焦點放在人生的喜悅上 , 或是現在主義者──這並不重要 , 你的人生是受控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 「 未來導向 」 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者你也可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 生命在死亡之後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的彈性 , 以使思維轉換視角 , 流暢地依情況的需求而定 , 這才是你要學會的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以很快地 , 最好的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度未來的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	以及現代主義的調節 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低調的消極性和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的臨時混合就是你從過去的過去行為中所得到的正面能給你的根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來你能看到的是翅膀能翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	從現在的享樂主義得到的 , 是能量 , 是能量 , 是去探索你自己、地點、人、感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度的時光都比積極來得負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來要犧牲什麼才能成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友時間
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂時光 , 犧牲個人的安慰
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 。 犧牲了睡眠 。 所以這會影響到他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	並且為了工作、成就和控制生活
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信 , 與一些ted成員的共鳴
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	讓我產生共鳴 。 我小時候在南布朗克斯區貧民窟長大 , 一個西西里島家庭--所有人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我在這裡 , 是個朝前看的人 , 他們因為老師介入而做了這些犧牲 , 讓我有了未來的方向感 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你拿到兩顆 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了 「 暫停生命 」 , 我把重心放在過往正面 , 所以 , 在76歲 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正把這個方法用在許多世界問題上:改變學校的輟學率、結合癮、增強青少年健康、用時間隱喻來治療老年人的創傷後壓力症候群 , 用時間隱喻來治療奇蹟 , 提高永續性和保護 , 減少身體上的復健 , 在那裡有五十%的退學率、改變自殺式恐怖分子的念頭 , 以及修改家庭衝突的時間區 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說 , 生活中許多謎題都可以藉由了解你的時間角度和其他人的時間角度來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	當今的新聞頭條中有多少人在一百年後會很重要 ? 1000年 ? kirkcitron的《漫長新聞》專案計畫收集當今不只重要報導了幾十年後 , 甚至會在數世紀前發出回響 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調了有潛力塑造我們未來的頭條 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球性議題、媒體、新聞、科學
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcron:而現在 , 真正的新聞
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈350萬則新聞
that's just one source .	那只是一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:那些故事在長期來看 , 到底有多少是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	那就是 「 長遠新聞 」 背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是長久以來基金會的一個計畫 , 由tedsters成立 , 包括凱文凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的 , 是那些在五十或十萬年後仍然很重要的新聞故事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 順帶一提 , 還會大量下跌 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 從a.p.的頂尖故事中來看 , 這在十年內會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好 , 剛剛那還滿酷的 。
