but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年最頂尖的故事是經濟體系 , 我敢打賭 , 遲早 , 這種經濟衰退 , 將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 哪種故事可能對未來有所影響 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 讓我們把科學
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會經過我們的血液中 , 去修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 那一天早就來了
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液殺死腫瘤 ; 他們將基因送入大腦 ; 他們建造的機器人能在人體上爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何養活九十億人口 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	今天我們有60億人無法餵飽
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	不靠遺傳改造作物英國人會餓死
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾•蓋茲有十億人在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界在何時會變得非常不同 , 如果中國設定了議程 , 他們也可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們已經開始在兒童身上做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的事業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們尋找各種途徑來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:有一個來自阿根廷的蟻群 , 現在已經傳到每一個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自我導向的機器人科學家 , 很快的被發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也可能不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在十二萬年後被喚醒 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 有或沒有我們 , 生命會延續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但去年 , 我挑選的長篇新聞報導是這個:在月球上發現水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓整個群體放到上面更容易 ,
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果nasa不做 , 中國也可能 , 或在座的某人 , 可能會寫下很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家carolynporco顯示從卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 將焦點放在它最大的衛星 , 土衛六 , 及冰冷的土衛二上 , 這似乎是對冰產生的射擊聲 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 太空 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 圖像化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco讓我們飛到土星去
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我將帶大家踏上一段旅程
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	你和我已經踏上這趟旅程很多年了 , 五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不僅真的登上了月球 , 還把機器人發射到各個行星上 , 我們有八個發射器 , 我們在小行星上登陸 , 我們還與彗星相對抗 , 此時 , 我們有一台太空船正往冥王星運行 , 它還曾經被稱為行星的行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務都是人類更大的旅程中的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解一些事情 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的本源 , 以及地球 , 我們居住的地球 , 來到這裡 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系的所有地方 , 我們都可以去找尋答案 , 像這樣的問題 , 這是土星 。 我們在1980年代初期去過土星 。 但是我們對土星的研究 , 自卡西尼號太空船開始進行更深入的詳細研究 , 穿越行星空間 , 行經七年之久 , 行駛於土星的各個地方 , 2004年夏天 , 行駛於土星運行軌道上 , 成為當時人類到達地球最遠的機器人 , 在太陽周圍繞地球運行 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的科學洞見 , 並且很明顯的超出了對比之外的魅力 , 而這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙成就 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們能夠學到很多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的照片是andromedanebula , 這是我們銀河系中最接近、最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這是個漂亮的複合物 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程 , 其實也是一個比喻 , 象徵一個更大的人類旅程 , 來了解我們周遭所有事物的相互關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入那個畫面 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們和卡西尼一起學到了 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們在過去兩年半拍攝的所有美麗照片 , 因為我根本沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我要講的最令人興奮的故事 , 是從這個重大探索中所浮現出來的兩個 , 我們在土星進行的探險 , 並且已經進行了兩年半了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	伴隨土星由廣大而多樣的衛星組成
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	範圍從幾公里範圍到美國整體大小 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝過土星的美麗圖片事實上 , 與土星的衛星一起在土星上 。 這是土星和土衛二 , 土星和土星 , 再來看看環狀邊緣 , 顯示它有多薄 , 上面有土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	目前土星47顆衛星中有兩顆是固定的 ,
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些土衛六和土衛二 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裏 , 是我們在太陽系中最大的未被探索過的地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	長期以來人們一直對這些行星充滿著好奇心 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的地表環境被認為比較像是我們在地球上所存在的環境 , 至少過去曾是如此 , 比起太陽系裡的其他天體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣中含有大量氮分子 , 就像在座各位所呼吸的氮 , 只不過它的大氣層中充滿了簡單的有機物質 , 像是甲烷、丙烷、乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在土衛六的大氣中含有很高的含量 , 會被破解 , 而它們的產品會加入一起製造霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個霧狀物無處不在 , 完全是全球化和封閉的泰坦 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你無法用肉眼看到水面 , 在光譜的可見區域中 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 被保存下來 , 經過數十億年的時間 , 溫和地表溫和地表 , 覆蓋著厚厚的有機泥土 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像泰坦上的焦油 , 或者石油 , 或者我們不知道的一樣 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可能是土衛六地表溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷在土衛六上是多少水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是冷凝的 , 所以意識到這種情況給出了一個可能性的世界 。 你可以擁有甲烷雲 , ok , 在這些雲之上有幾百公里的霧狀物 , 這可以防止任何陽光無法到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度高達華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管那天寒冷 , 土衛六表面還是有可能會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 土衛六在地球上造成大雨:土衛二地雕刻地形 ; 它形成河流及白內障 ; 它能創造出峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石坑中進行水池 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥漿從高山和山丘上沖下山 , 再進入低地 , 停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	嘗試去想像土衛六的表面長什麼樣子
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	那裡一片漆黑 。 泰坦上一片漆黑 , 跟地球上一片漆黑一樣 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡天寒地凍 , 陰森恐怖 , 迷霧重重 , 可能正在下雨 , 你可能正站在密西根湖邊 , 邊緣穿著油漆薄荷 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號到達卡西尼號之前所發現的景象 。 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上所發現的 , 雖然在細節上不盡相同 , 但卻和那個故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 卡西尼號就好像是叢羅爾斯•凡爾納的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	就像我說的 , 它有很厚、很廣的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是土衛六 , 被太陽照亮 , 光環盡可能地呈現美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	而那裡是另一顆衛星--我甚至不知道它是哪一個 , 它是一個非常廣大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器可以透過大氣層看到水面 , 我的攝影機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了這張照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 對我們來說 , 差不多就這麼大了 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在太神秘了:我們無法知道我們在土衛六上看到的是什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你更仔細地觀察這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些像sipous般的頻道--我們不知道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上是隕石坑 , 但是土衛六表面的隕石坑數量很少 , 意思是說 , 它是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	而且有著看似板塊的特徵
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到行星上有線性的東西 , 它意味著有分裂 , 像個斷層一樣 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	由此可經由地質變換
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理會我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一件事件發生了 , 許多人認為卡西尼號的高峰事件 , 是針對土衛六的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲的製造業的惠更斯號探測器 , 卡西尼號在太陽系中進行了七年 。 我們把這個探測器部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 它花了兩個半小時才降落 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只是想強調一個事件有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外太陽系的領域中首次登陸 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這在我心目中是如此重大 , 這個事件本來應該要與美國各地的街頭遊行和歐洲讚揚 , 可悲的是 , 並不是這樣 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	另一個原因也很明顯 。 這是國際的使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國都被讚頌 , 而慶祝的口音是用英語的口音 , 美國的口音 , 及德語的口音 , 還有法語、法語、意大利式和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是一場關於 「 聯合國 」 的即時演示 , 應該要表達的意思是:一個真正的國度團結在一起 , 一起努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探索行星是一個巨大的任務 , 去理解一個行星系統 , 這個行星在人類歷史上一直無法達成 , 而現在人類真的碰觸到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	我是說 , 我開始起雞皮疙瘩 ,
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 也是我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不應該 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但不管怎樣 , 探測器在降下過程中對大氣進行了測量 , 也拍了全景圖 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你第一次看到土衛六地表的照片是什麼感覺 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這讓人震驚 , 因為我們希望從軌道上拍下的所有照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是個很明顯的模式 , 地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	一種只靠液體流動才能形成的樹狀滴狀模式 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些管道 , 看出它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們匯聚到這裡的這個通道 , 這個通道滲透到這個地區 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你現在看到的是一條海岸線 ,
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片拍攝於16公里
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是在8公里範圍拍攝的照片 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你搭乘飛機橫跨美國 , 你就是在高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是鐵達尼亞航空公司穿越鐵達尼號的窗戶 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在水面來來去休息 , 我要給各位看 , 各位先生女士 , 第一次從外太陽系的月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些很可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對吧 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在了其中一塊平坦、深色的區域 , 且它沒有沉沒消失 。 所以它不是我們落入的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器找到的 , 基本上是土衛六相當於一塊泥土平坦 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是由液態甲烷構成的未解體
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	很有可能這種材料能透過我們看到的這些通道 , 將土衛六的高地沖刷走 , 讓它排水超過數十億年 , 來填補低窪地帶的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然 , 我們的影像中沒有標語 , 甚至是在惠更斯號圖像中 , 沒有大型的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 這個問題變得更加令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們拍攝土衛六赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是100公尺高 , 被幾公里高的沙丘 , 它們會繼續上好幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有幾百到一千到一千二百英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	它顯然是個非常乾燥的地方 , 否則不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 又再一次 , 牠感到疑惑 , 沒有任何液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	那裡有一座位於南極地帶的湖
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大小和安大略湖差不多 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 大約一週半前 , 我們飛過北極 , 發現了加勒比海的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 為了某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少這個季節 , 很明顯地 , 土衛六的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們應該會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個很了不起的地方 , 很神秘 , 很奇特 , 卻也很外星人 , 但也很奇怪地 , 且有著像地球的地質構造 , 以及很棒的地理多樣性 , 且是個很炫的世界 , 在太陽系中 , 只有複雜性和豐富性的世界 , 是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二看看 , 土衛二是個小衛星 , 大小約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以在英格蘭的旁邊看到 , 只是要讓你們知道它的大小 。 土衛二是個威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常耀眼 , 它的表面很明顯是破裂的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	這是一個非常地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多存在於南極而我們在這個南極點發現了碎裂的系統
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	而它們是不同的顏色因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被塗滿 。 這些碎片塗滿了有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個南極區域還提升了溫度 , 這是地球上最熱最熱的區域 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就和發現地球的南極還要熱帶地方一樣奇特 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 我們拍攝了更多的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些裂痕上 , 噴射出細小的冰粒 , 噴射範圍長達數百英里 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們將這個影像上色 , 想讓它有微弱的光線升高 , 我們就看到這些噴流在土衛二的空中 , 我們看到 , 在其他的影像中 , 能走上數千英里 , 進入土衛二的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊對這些圖片進行了檢驗 , 就像這張圖片 , 考慮到來自卡西尼號的另一個結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是 , 這些噴流可能是由土衛二地表下的液態水孔所噴發而出 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有的 , 可能是液態水 , 有機物質和過剩的熱量 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們很可能發現了現代地球探索的聖杯 。 也就是說 , 一個可能適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴你們 , 我們太陽系中其他地方生物的發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有巨大的文化與科學上的影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能展示出過去的機率 , 不只一次 , 而是兩次 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 按照慣例 , 它在整個宇宙和它的歷史上已經發生了很驚人的次數 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍是唯一一顆充滿生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它很獨特 , 到目前為止 , 它仍然是我們唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們之中有人在1960年代時保持警覺和連貫性的話我們會原諒你 , 如果你沒看好你會記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人拍下的這張著名的照片
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空拍攝的地球 , 它對於我們在宇宙中所處的位置產生了巨大的影響 , 我們對於保護地球的責任感也產生了巨大的影響 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼號同樣拍下了一張前所未見的人類眼睛
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是日全蝕 , 從土星的另一側可以看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張無與倫比的照片中 , 你看到背著太陽的主要光環 , 你看到太陽折射後的影像 , 你看到土衛二的光環 , 事實上是來自土衛二的表面 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠精彩 , 我們可以在這美麗的圖像中找到 , 看得到我們自己的星球 , 在土星光環的臂彎中搜尋 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	看到我們自己深深地感動 , 捕捉到我們在其他世界的小藍西行星 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	那個 , 還有我們自己從中獲益的觀點 , 可能最後會是我們從這次長達半個世紀的探索之中所獲得的最好的獎勵 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	直到2005年 , 全球只剩下15%的人被繪製出來 。 這減緩了災難後的援助並隱藏了尚未使用的土地和未知的公路的經濟潛力 。 在這簡短的演講中 , google的laliteskatragadademos地圖製作者 , 一個團體繪製地圖的工具是全世界的人都在使用地圖繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	laliteshkatragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建構經濟
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 氣旋納吉斯破壞了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需援助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人趕到這個區域
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖、沒有道路的地圖、沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 也沒有辦法幫到氣旋受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地區的地圖達到可計算的程度 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國與世界大部分的居民遭遇了一個問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救援終於來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google有40位志願者使用了一套新的軟體標註了12萬公里的道路3000間醫院 , 後勤和救護站
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一個能賦予我們每個人力量的科技 , 能讓我們在地圖上繪製我們已知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們使用這套軟體標註了所有道路 , 河流 , 從學校 , 到當地企業 , 還有錄影帶店 , 到角落的店家 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名人hernandodesto認爲開發中國家要實現經濟效益的關鍵在於利用大量未被破壞的土地
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 僅在印度就有一兆美元的房地產仍然未被列入控管 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 就有170個國家的成千上萬的使用者就標註了幾百萬筆資訊 , 做出了一張前所未有的詳細資訊地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這一切都要靠熱情的使用者力量才能實現 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看目前用戶所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 我們在談話的同時 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們正在繪製這個世界的地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛剛為塞內加爾標註了一條路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家比較近 , 查盧亞是班加羅爾的ng道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學的結果 , 手勢以及機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數百個用戶的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個用戶 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們70%未被開發的星球邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村莊一場10個月的非暴力抗議活動 , 阻止一個橫跨橄欖叢林的阻礙 。 你們有聽過嗎 ? 不這麼認為 。 巴西製片家族製造商茱莉亞.巴哈查問為什麼我們只注意在以色列衝突中的暴力 , 而不是沒有暴力的領袖有一天可以帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞•巴哈:注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的工作 , 他們試圖用和平手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總是會問一個問題:巴勒斯坦大甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我通常是從中東回來的 , 我在那裡花時間拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 他們來自以色列士兵和居民 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試著要鑄造一個全國大規模的非暴力運動 , 來結束這個地區的佔領並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 你們多數人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分歧存在於地面上的情況和國外的感知之間 , 是我們還沒有成為巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動成功的主要原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天在這裡要談的是關注的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及非暴力運動的出現與發展 , 在西岸 , 加薩 , 及其他地方 , 但現今 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 成長所缺乏的 , 絕大部分的原因 , 並不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力的方式 , 而是讓我們開始注意到已經在使用的那些人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我藉由帶你們到這個名為布德魯斯的村落來說明這個觀點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種的危機 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建造一個隔閡 , 而部分障礙會蓋在村莊的上面 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 並且被包圍著 , 所以他們會失去使用權的免費途徑 , 來到西岸的其他地方 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地領導人的鼓舞 , 他們發動了和平反抗運動 , 來阻止這發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的片段 , 你們可以了解在地表上實際上長什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知圍牆會把巴勒斯坦和以色列分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯 , 我們發現這道牆將竊取我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男性:這道圍籬事實上對恐怖主義提出了一個解決之道
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男性:今天你被邀請去和平的遊行
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位你的以色列兄弟姐妹
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:沒有什麼事情比非暴力抗爭更嚇人 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女性:我們看見男人試圖推動士兵但他們都不能夠這樣做
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女生也可以
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須空空想著傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們完全處於和諧中 , 我們想要把它傳播到全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號聲:一國一國歌
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和流行的前身 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:籬笆上方的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來驅散群眾
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們可以使用任何必要的武力
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活生生的子彈
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就像fallujah一樣 , 到處拍攝
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列激進份子:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但 , 我身邊還有一些人甚至不畏縮 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭是無法阻止其發生的 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們做得到 ! 我們可以辦到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	茱莉亞•巴夏:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體並沒有報導這一連串非凡的事件 , 這件事發生在七年前 , 2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更讓人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 經過了十個月的和平反抗 , 說服了以色列政府將這道屏障搬離他們的土地 , 移到綠線上 , 也就是國際公認的以色列與巴勒斯坦領土之間的疆界 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此傳遍整個西岸的村子以及耶路撒冷境內巴勒斯坦的街坊
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體還是沈默著這些故事 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會帶來很深遠的後果 , 讓非暴力行為能夠成長的可能性變大 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦出現 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點 , 他們都是劇院的一種形式 , 來向觀眾致力 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷拿到頭版並引起國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題非暴力領袖就很難向他們的社群宣揚公民不服從是可行的選擇來處理他們的困境
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	關注的力量或許會讓在場的父母親們大吃一驚
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	若要讓你的孩子能夠更大聲丟出蟻虎 , 最好的方式就是讓他注意他第一次丟出一個健身房 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	螞蟻會成為童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子們學到了 , 他可以藉此得到父母親的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能透過給予或吸引孩子注意力來獎勵或減輕父母的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為都可能受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇要把注意力放在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信結束中東地區的衝突的核心以及帶動和平的目的是要讓我們將非暴力行為轉化為一個功能性行為 , 透過讓更多關注到現今在地面上的非暴力領袖 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的影片的過程中 , 拍攝約旦河西岸的村子 , 在加薩 , 以及東耶路撒冷的村子 , 我看到了就算只是一部紀錄片也能影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個名叫瓦拉杰的村子裡 , 坐落在離耶路撒冷很近的村子裡 , 這個社區面臨跟布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 無法取得的自由 , 不論是到西岸還是耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力手段大約兩年了 , 但因為沒人關注他們 , 他們漸漸被取消 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一項篩選 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後他們舉辦了目前為止最有熱忱且有紀律的示威遊行
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	主辦人說村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在影片中 , 感覺確實有人在跟隨他們正在做的事情 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列那邊 , 有一場新的和平運動 , 叫做solicariot , 它在希伯來語中表示團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領袖一直在用布德鲁斯村作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導說 , 那些從來沒有參與過的以色列人他們看到影片 , 了解非暴力的力量並開始加入他們的活動
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰村和索里德拉爾特的案例顯示即使是一部小成本的獨立製片也能夠將非暴力變成一個功能性行為
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家能夠擁有的力量 , 只要他們開始報導每週在村子裡發生的非暴力事件 , 如比爾、尼因亞、瓦拉杰區 , 在耶路撒冷的社區裡 , 像是希克•傑拉哈和西里爾 , 非暴力領導人就更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要去理解 , 如果我們不去注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 而且好像它們從來沒有發生過那樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見到如果我們有 , 他們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們加起來 , 他們的影響會在以色列巴勒斯坦的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的就是那種影響力 , 終於能夠解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明了非暴力是可行的 , 在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們關注這些問題 , 讓他們證明它在任何地方都行得通 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•塞尚有一個簡單但強大的模式 , 針對激勵人心的領導力 , 都是從一個金色圓圈開始 , 問題是 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金 , 及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售量 , 成功的銷售 ,
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•奈克:偉大領袖如何激發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要怎麼解釋當事情不如我們所設想的時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠實現似乎違背所有假設的時候 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們的創新比他們所有的競爭都還要多 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 ,
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才華、同樣的機構、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼 , 為什麼他們似乎有什麼不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁•路德•金恩領導黑人民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的男人 , 他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出控制力、有權力的人飛行 , 卻有其他團隊更符合資格、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	而且他們沒有達到人力飛機的目的 , 萊特兄弟則打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我做了一個發現
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對於世界運作方式的看法 , 甚至深深改變了我在其中運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	事實證明 , 所有偉大而鼓舞人心的領袖及世界上的組織不管是蘋果電腦 , 或馬丁路德金恩或萊特兄弟他們都以同樣的方式去思考、行動與溝通
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且完全與其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是將其編碼 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和有些領袖能夠激發出其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你稱它為不同的價值主張 , 你的屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少有個人或組織 , 知道他們為什麼要做他們的工作 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我說的 「 為什麼 」 指的不是 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 , 永遠是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的理由是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼會存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	還有 , 為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	嗯 , 結果是 , 我們的思考 , 我們的行為 , 我們的溝通方式是從外而內的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這是顯而易見的 。 我們從最清晰的東西 , 到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人心的領導人和激勵人心的組織不管它們的規模 , 不管它們的產業都從內而外的都去思考、行動與溝通
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦是因為它們很容易了解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能會聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造了很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很美 , 很容易使用 , 也很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? " 嗯.. "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方式 , 多數業務都是這樣進行的 , 而這是多數人與人之間的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何比較好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買行為、投票之類的 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律事務所:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶 , 和我們一起做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很好的氣體哩程 , 它有皮革製的座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	以下是蘋果電腦實際上溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 相信挑戰現狀 ,
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是使我們的產品有美好的設計、容易使用、友好使用的產品 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧做出了不起的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你準備好向我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是逆轉訊息的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是 , 人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們會買你為什麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在場的每一位購買蘋果電腦都很舒服 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很盡力從蘋果電腦買到mp3播放器 , 或蘋果的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能把它們和它們的競爭者區別開來 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都有同樣資格去製造所有這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面螢幕電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯很有資格可以做平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在做平面螢幕監測 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	dell帶著mp3的球員和pdas出櫃 , 他們製造出很棒的品質產品 , 他們能做出完美設計的產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在談到這個話題 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你有什麼的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你所相信的人們做生意
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	以下是最棒的部分:我告訴各位的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都是基於生物學的萬靈丹 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的橫切面 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦實際上是被切成了三個主要部份 , 和黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的腦 , 我們的智人腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 對應的是 「 什麼 」 的層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦新皮質負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩區構成我們的邊緣腦 , 我們的邊緣腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也要為所有人類的行為 , 所有決策負責 , 它也沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內地溝通時是的 , 人們可以理解很多複雜的資訊量像是特色、好處、事實和數字
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它就是不能驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內在溝通 , 我們就直接對著大腦控制行為的那部份進行交流 , 然後我們讓人們能夠合理化它 , 用我們說的有形的東西去做 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道選擇的來源
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時 , 你可以給人所有的事實和數據 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節 , 但感覺就是不對勁 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用那個動詞 , 它不會是 「 感覺 」 的 , 對吧 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦並不能控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最多能整理出的就是: 「 我不知道 , 就是覺得不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你說你以心為領導 , 或是你帶著靈魂去領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想讓你們知道 , 這些都不是身體的其他部位在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣腦中 , 是控制決策而不是語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼做你該做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼做你該做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們去投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠一點 , 想要成為你正在做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不是只是要賣給需要你有什麼的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的人們
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人僅是因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢而工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人 , 他們會為你工作 , 讓你流血、流汗、流淚 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有比萊特兄弟更好的例子了
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回顧二十世紀初期 , 追求有權力的人飛機就像是當天的網路部隊 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有 , 我們假設的成功的關鍵
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你去問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或是你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三樣東西:資本化、錯誤的人、市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是同一三件事 , 所以我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley在戰爭部門給5萬美金來搞清楚這個飛行機器
money was no problem .	錢都沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他擁有哈佛大學的一席 , 在史密森納工作 , 並且有非常良好的聯繫 ; 他知道當時所有的大眾心智 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的頭腦資金 , 市場狀況很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都為langley加油 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠在俄亥俄州 , 歐維爾和威爾伯特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功的配方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用腳踏車店的價格支付他們的夢想 ; 沒有一個人在萊特兄弟的隊伍中 , 受過大學教育 , 甚至沒有奧維爾或威爾伯 ; 而紐約時報也跟著他們到處跑 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同的是 , 奧維爾和威爾伯被一個目的、一個目的、一個信念所驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這架飛行機器這將改變世界的軌道
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他想成名
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人時
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟夢想的人用血汗與淚水與他們一同努力
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另一些人只是為錢工作 ,
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是每次萊特兄弟出門他們就得帶上五套零件因為這是他們出門前會墜機的次數
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟起飛 , 甚至沒有人去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley是錯的動機那天萊特兄弟起飛了 , 放棄了
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 各位 , 這是很驚人的發現 , 我會改進你們的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他退出 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們是重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	有種東西叫做創新法則 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你肯定知道這個術語是術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口都是我們的創新者
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%都是我們的早期採用者
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數 , 晚期的大多數以及落後者 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式手機的唯一原因 , 就是因為你不能再買轉子電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	在這個尺度上我們都坐在不同的地方 , 但創新的散佈法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你不可能擁有它 , 直到你達到了這個臨界點 , 在15%到18%之間 , 市場的滲透率接近到這個系統的尖端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 大概是10%吧 。 」 很驕傲的 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 可以讓超過百分之十的客戶絆倒 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人說 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何形容他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就像是那種直覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是拿到的 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 找到那些得到的 ? 與那些沒有得到它的人做比較 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以就是這個 , 這個小小的差距你必須結束 , 正如jeffreymoore所說的 , 「 跨越隔閡 」 因為 , 你看 , 早期的大多數人都不會嘗試直到其他人首先嘗試為止
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 革新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很放心可以做出那些直覺的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們對做這些直覺的決定感到更為自在 , 被他們對世界的信念所驅使 , 而不僅僅只是可得的東西 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是排隊排了六小時買iphone的人 , 他們一開始出去買 , 一週後你可以走進店裡 , 在架子上買一台iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人一開始花四萬美元在平面螢幕電視上即使科技是次要的
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	而且 , 順帶一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術非常棒 , 他們自己也這麼做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要先
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼就證明了你相信什麼
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做證明自己相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人買iphone的原因在前六小時 , 排隊排了六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們希望每個人如何看待他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	所以讓我舉一個有名的例子一個有名的失敗以及有名的成功關於創新法則的散播
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 有名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們之前所說 , 一秒鐘前成功的秘訣就是金錢和對的人以及對的市場狀況 , 對嗎 ? 你那時應該有成功的
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	在tivo上市的時間 , 大概是八、九年前 , 到現在 , 它們是市場上唯一高品質的產品 , 手下來 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們是非常有錢的 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場狀況很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo當作動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我常把東西綁在垃圾筒裡 , 華納的dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但是tivo卻失敗了
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo , 他們的股價約30到40美元 , 然後跌倒 , 從沒在10美元以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它會在6歲以上進行交易 , 除了幾項小漲幅 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們有的是什麼
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個可以暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過商業廣告 , 改掉現場電視 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 你甚至不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 , 我們不喜歡
you're scaring us . "	你嚇壞了我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控生活各個層面的人 , 那我們有給你的產品 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它能暫停現場電視 , 跳過商業廣告 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼就只是你相信的證明
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子關於關於創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出去沒有邀請 , 也沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人在美國公民權利上受苦
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國什麼需要改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	還有那些相信他所相信的人們接受了他的理念 , 並且他們自己動手做 , 並且告訴人們
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓大家能接納更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	大家看 , 25萬人出現在對的日子 , 聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	是他們所相信的美國使他們在八月中時搭乘巴士穿梭於華盛頓的陽光之中 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 這不是關於黑人與白人25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種類型的法律:那些由較高權威制定的法律 , 以及那些由人類所定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由人類所定的法律都與那些高權威制定的法律一致時我們才活在一個公正的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	公民權運動正是幫助他奪走生命的完美之處 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順道一提 , 他還給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽現在的政治人物 , 有他們完整的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者和領導者
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位階但那些領導的人啟發我們
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論他們是個人或組織 , 我們會追隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們而是為了我們自己
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	就是那些以 「 為何 」 開頭的人 , 具有啟發他們周圍的人的能力 , 或是去找激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼還記得你把車子停哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是朝對的方向前進 ? 神經科學家尼爾伯格研究出繪出我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 以及他們如何連結到記憶與想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索神經科學、科學
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburgess:你的大腦如何告訴你你所在的位置 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們把車停在一個大停車場 , 我們怎麼記住車子停在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面臨的問題是:
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	然後我們會試著去了解他的大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從黃色標示海馬體開始也就是記憶的器官
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損傷 , 像是阿茲海默症 , 你記不起什麼東西 , 包括你把車子停哪 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文 " 海馬 " 所命名的 , 它的相似性 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元所組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人腦中有大約一千億個神經元
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會彼此溝通 , 做法是發送小脈衝或尖刺的電流 , 透過彼此的連結來溝通 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞彼此非常緊密的連接組成
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的藉由記錄老鼠在旅行時記錄老鼠或在尋找食物時的個別神經元
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以我們會想像我們記錄一個單一神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體裡面
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一個電的尖刺時 , 將會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到這個神經元知道老鼠在環境中的某一個特定地方
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會藉由發送電流尖刺傳送訊號給大腦其他部位 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以展示神經元的發射率 , 作為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中紀錄我們會發現當不同神經元在不同部位的環境中發射出訊號例如在這個方形的盒子裡
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起 , 組成一張大腦地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中的哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被人類紀錄進去 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲讓他們在小鎮上開車
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	當他們開車經過某個地方時 , 海馬體裡的位置細胞會被激發 , 開始發出電子脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人在環境中的位置呢 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的邊界是特別重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	頂部的那個喜歡打火 , 可以說是兩隻老鼠在盒子裡之間的中間 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你將盒子的空間擴大時 , 激發的位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面那個則是每當南方靠近一面牆的時候會開火 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子裡放置另一面牆 , 那麼細胞在兩個地方都會被激發 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 , 南方隨處可見一面牆 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這推測 , 去感應你周圍環境的距離和方向 , 來感應你周圍的邊界 , 建築物等等 , 對於海馬體是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在輸入海馬體的同時 , 海馬體上的細胞發現哪個細胞被投射到海馬體上 , 海馬體的確會在特定的距離或邊緣來回應從老鼠或老鼠的四處移動 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近一面牆的時候 , 它會被激發 , 或向東偏 , 不論是方形的或是圓形的牆 , 甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物都在四處奔跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞每次都激發出南方的界線 , 不論是桌子的邊緣或是牆壁的邊緣或是兩張桌子的間隙 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以這就是我們認為位置細胞可以決定動物所在的方位 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物品的位置 , 像是這個目標旗子 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或者說 , 你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	因此我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 去看看他們必須記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把他們放回環境中 , 通常他們很擅長把馬克筆放在他們認為旗子或車子的位置上 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞所做的實驗一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看出他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變的 , 看你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗幟位於一個小廣場的環境中 , 然後如果你問人那裡的位置 , 就會讓環境變大 , 他們認為旗幟的位置會跟那裡的位置一樣 , 一直延伸出去 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好比你還記得旗幟的位置 , 藉著儲存所有位置細胞的模式在你所在位置的位置 , 然後你可以藉由四處移動來回到那個位置 , 這樣你就最好配合你所在的位置細胞被激發的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那引導你回到你想記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也透過動作知道我們在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們選擇了一些不受限制的路徑也許我們會停車離開我們知道因為我們自己的動作我們可以整合這條路徑大約是前進的方向
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從稱為 「 網格細胞 」 的細胞中得到這種整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	同樣的 , 網格細胞也被找到來輸入海馬體 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處移動的時候每個細胞會激發一系列不同的位置在一個非常規的三角形網格
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你紀錄數個網格細胞以不同的顏色標記在這裡每個細胞都有一個網格狀的激發模式在整個環境中每一個細胞的網格激發模式都被略過相對於其他細胞
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	圖中的紅色部分會發射綠色部分就是藍色的部分
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 把這隻老鼠放在一起 , 就好像這隻老鼠能在周遭環境放置一個虛擬的網格 , 有點像地圖上所看到的緯度和長度的線 , 但是用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	隨著它四處移動 , 電流活動能從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 持續追蹤自己的所在 , 如此一來 , 它就能用它自己的移動來知道自己在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有網格狀的對稱性都有相同的對稱性 , 同樣的對稱軸 , 在這裡用橘色表示 , 網格細胞的網格活動 , 大腦的特定區域都應該根據這六個方向流動 , 或六個方向之間的轉向來改變 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進磁共振成像掃描儀 , 讓他們做一個像我剛剛給你們看的電玩遊戲並尋找這訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你確實在人腦內看到的是同一個部位於老鼠腦內的網格細胞
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得車子的位置在他車子的位置和方向 , 來延伸出去 , 建物和界線就在他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	可以用邊界偵測細胞來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他從公園拿出的路徑 , 這路徑會用網格細胞的頂端表示 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞被激發
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動找到他正在停車的位置 , 找到目前位置和他大腦中儲存的位置模式 , 來回到當初車子停放的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這就引導他回到那個地點 , 對視覺的不尊重 , 像是他的車子是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許已經開始倒閉了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道去哪就得到了 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶體外 , 如果我們觀察大腦內部的網格狀激發模式 , 我們會看到一系列的位置會一直活躍起來 , 當我們在做各種自傳記憶工作時 , 比如說 , 記住你上次參加婚禮時的那些地方 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以這可能是神經機制代表著我們周圍的空間也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能在空間中重現空間的景象 , 至少在我們想要想像的時候 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果發生了這些 , 你的記憶就能夠從位置細胞開始 , 藉由這些密集的互相連結來啟動彼此 , 接著重新啟動了界限細胞 , 創造出圍繞在你的視線周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以藉由這個空間來移動這個視野
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種我還沒提過的細胞頭向細胞 , 它們就像是指南針一樣根據面向不同的方向而激發 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	它們可以定義視覺的方向 , 可以讓你產生影像 , 以視覺的影像為例 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮上 , 會發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以 , 這只是一個新時代的例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 像是你如何去記憶、想像 , 甚至是以數十億個神經元組成的作用來思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個由全球安全驅動的全球安全局、政府、私部門和民眾攜手合作 。 那不僅是開放式工作扇門的遠景 , 也是北大西洋公約組織的最高指揮官 。 他對將來在近期軍事史上共享生存的景象 , 解釋為何要打造橋樑而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球性議題、開放性議題、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯塔瓦里迪斯:北約的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 ?
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要稍微談一下開放資源的安全性 , 因為我們在這21世紀 , 必須要做得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先回顧一下20世紀吧 , 稍微了解安全這個風格對我們有多有效 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北邊 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在verdun , 1916年 , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人被殺 , 所以一天大約兩千人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	若你將它向前轉二十世紀安全進到二次世界大戰 , 你看到在斯大林格勒的戰役 , 300天 , 2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬蓋諾防線 , 然後進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	今天我要告訴大家的是 , 與其建造牆壁來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這座橋在drina河上 , 由ivoandrikic所寫的小說的主題 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹地區非常困擾的部分 , 隨著時間的推移 , 都會有巨大的建築物 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	近十年來 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫不決地 , 團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會再次強調 , 開放式安全是關聯國際間、跨部門、私人和公共的關係 , 並與策略性溝通 , 大致上都是在社交網上進行 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物正在以各種方式受到攻擊 , 且對全球公有物的威脅都不會因為建造圍牆而受到威脅 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是一個水手 , 很顯然
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 裝設線 , 橫越印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張圖有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	沿著它的側邊裝著導電纜線 ,
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	也就是避免海盜襲擊它
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	盜版是現今全球都非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也在馬拉加海峽非常活躍
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	在幾內亞灣活躍
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到的
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球交通運輸系統中 , 每年美金一百億美元的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500名船員被挾持著 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何去處理
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網絡海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩個年輕男子的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	在當下 , 他們被監禁著 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們進行了信用卡詐騙案 , 並且以超過一百億美元的身價淨利 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分這是全球經濟不連續2兆美金的一部分
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的國內生產毛額下
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這片網路海 , 我們無止境地瞭解它是激進開放的基本面向 , 它也受到威脅 。
